If/when spawn logic grows past ~50 lines (multiple unit types, randomized positions, AI starting army, etc. — Phase 3+), extract to `scripts/match_setup.gd` attached as a child of Main in main.tscn. Per CLAUDE.md "Escalation" rule #1: implementation choice, prefer simplest option, document briefly.

- **Five starting Kargars vs. the canonical three.** 01_CORE_MECHANICS.md §2 step 1 specifies "each player starts with one Throne building, three workers, and the hero." Wave 2 ships 5 — purely for click-target ergonomics during ui-developer's SelectionManager testing (more units = more visible click events when stress-testing the selection ring + right-click-move flow). The number lives in `_KARGAR_SPAWN_POSITIONS` (a const Array[Vector3] in main.gd), NOT in BalanceData or Constants — it's a UX-of-testing knob, not a balance value, and it disappears when the canonical 3-worker start lands with the resource economy in Phase 3. Per CLAUDE.md "Escalation" rule #1 — implementation choice with no gameplay effect (no economy yet, the workers can't gather), no QUESTIONS_FOR_DESIGN.md entry needed. Will be reconsidered in Phase 3 when the economy makes the count load-bearing.

- **`main.gd` calls `Unit.reset_id_counter()` via path-string-preloaded `_UnitScript` ref.** Same registry-race reason kargar.gd uses path-string extends. main.gd is the root scene script — it's parsed at scene-boot, the same window where `Unit` may not yet be in the global class_name registry. Reflective `_UnitScript.call(&"reset_id_counter")` works regardless. The reset is needed so unit_ids deterministically run 1..5 across runs (replay-diff cleanliness, snapshot test stability) — `MatchHarness.start_match` already calls this internally, but the live boot path doesn't go through MatchHarness, so the call is duplicated here. When a future `MatchSetup` script lands it'll absorb this responsibility.

- **kargar.tscn material is `Color(0.65, 0.5, 0.3)` (sandy brown), distinct from unit.tscn's `Color(0.3, 0.5, 0.7)` (blue-grey).** Color choice driven by the Shahnameh-rooted "worker of the soil" framing (01_CORE_MECHANICS.md §6 + the recurring "people of the land" theme in the source material). At placeholder fidelity the only requirement is "visually distinct from other unit silhouettes"; the brown does that against the future blue-grey infantry / red/orange Turan units / glowing Rostam. Test `test_kargar_material_is_brown_not_blue_grey` asserts the channel-by-channel signature (red high, blue low) without pinning exact values, so future tweaks can tune within the brown family without test churn. Per CLAUDE.md placeholder policy — colored shapes only, no real art until MVP loop is fun.

- **What did not ship in wave 2** (intentionally out of scope per the kickoff prompt): Other unit types (Piyade, Kamandar, Savar, Asb-savar, Rostam) — Phase 1 session 2 onward. Production buildings, costs spent on spawn — Phase 3 (resource economy). Combat behavior, attack range, damage — Phase 2. Worker gathering / construction / repair — Phase 3 (resource node interactions). Dying state visuals (death animation, fade out) — Phase 2 with combat. UnitState_Idle / UnitState_Moving — ai-engineer wave 2 (separately shipped this same wave). The 4 deliverable boxes from the wave-2 brief: Kargar class+scene ✅, 5-Kargar spawn in main.gd ✅, ARCHITECTURE.md §2 update (Kargar + Match start spawn rows) ✅, BUILD_LOG.md wave-2 entry ✅.

---

### v0.13.0 — Phase 1 Session 1 wave 2 (2026-05-01) — ai-engineer (Idle / Moving states)

- **`UnitState_Idle` and `UnitState_Moving` registered by the `Unit` base class, not by concrete subclasses.** State Machine Contract §3.1 says "Every State instance for a unit is allocated at spawn (in the unit's `_ready`)." The kickoff doc proposed concrete `Kargar`-style subclasses register their own states; the base class registers Idle and Moving (the universally-useful pair) so every concrete unit type ships with a working FSM out of the box. Subclasses that want extra states (Gathering for workers, Attacking for combatants, etc.) call `fsm.register(...)` BEFORE chaining to `super._ready()`. The base's `_ready` then idempotently registers Idle/Moving (only if not already present) and calls `init(&"idle")` only if `current` is still null. Rationale: this minimizes the boilerplate concrete subclasses repeat (gameplay-systems' `Kargar` doesn't have to know about Idle/Moving) and matches engine-architect's wave-1 retro note "If [Unit] does [register stub states], your job is just to make the actual UnitState subclasses exist and be findable."

- **`UnitState_Idle` / `UnitState_Moving` extend `unit_state.gd` by path-string, NOT by `class_name UnitState`.** Same project-wide class_name registry race (§6 v0.4.0, v0.9.0). Initial `extends UnitState` triggered the cascade where unit.gd's `class_name Unit` failed to register, surfacing as `Invalid call. Nonexistent function 'reset_id_counter (via call)' in base 'GDScript'` and `Invalid assignment of property or key 'unit_type' on a base object of type 'CharacterBody3D'` in test fixtures. Path-string base + `class_name UnitState_Idle` / `class_name UnitState_Moving` retained for typed external references. Unit also references the state scripts via path-string preload (`const _UnitStateIdleScript: Script = preload(...)`) instead of by class_name to dodge the same race when unit.gd is loaded in test contexts.

- **`StateMachine.transition_to_next` stashes the dispatched Command's kind/payload on `ctx.current_command` before returning the Command to the pool.** State Machine Contract §3.4 explicitly leaves this open: "the popped command is returned, so concrete states must read their target from elsewhere (e.g., ctx.current_command — to be defined when concrete states ship)." Wave 2 ships the definition: `Unit.current_command: Dictionary = {}` with shape `{ "kind": StringName, "payload": Dictionary }`. The `StateMachine.transition_to_next` writes a defensive `payload.duplicate()` copy (so pool re-rent doesn't race), then returns the Command to the pool, then transitions. `_clear_current_command()` runs on the empty-queue → Idle path so a stale payload never leaks into Idle's tick. UnitState_Moving's `enter` reads `ctx.current_command.payload.target` — the StateMachine framework remains the single dispatcher; states read off the stashed dictionary.

- **`UnitState_Moving._sim_tick` drives `MovementComponent._sim_tick(dt)` directly.** Until the MovementSystem phase coordinator lands (a LATER item per wave-1 retro: "MovementSystem phase coordinator wiring"), Moving IS the per-tick driver for the MovementComponent. When the coordinator ships, it iterates registered MovementComponents during the `movement` phase and calls their `_sim_tick`; Moving's `_sim_tick` drops the explicit drive-call and just polls `path_state` / `is_moving`. This is a one-line refactor and is documented in both the source code (`unit_state_moving.gd` block comment above `_sim_tick`) and in the BUILD_LOG wave-2 retro under LATER items.

- **Arrival detection uses an `_arrival_pending` latch flipped on first READY observation, NOT on first `is_moving == true` observation.** Initial design used `is_moving == true` as the latch trigger, but in single-tick-arrival cases (huge `move_speed`, short distance, e.g. the test scenario `move_speed=100, target=(1,0,0)`) the MovementComponent ingests waypoints, advances position, and sets `_waypoint_index = waypoints.size()` all within a single `_sim_tick` call — so Moving never observes `is_moving == true`. Switched to `path_state == READY` as the latch trigger. The latch closes the "have a path" race correctly: Moving's `enter()` issues `request_repath` but the scheduler is non-blocking, so on the entry tick `is_moving` is false because no waypoints exist yet. Without the latch we'd transition back to Idle on the entry tick, never having moved. The READY-as-latch trigger handles both the single-tick and multi-tick arrival cases uniformly. Tests `test_moving_transitions_to_idle_on_arrival` and `test_full_idle_moving_idle_cycle` pin both shapes.

- **`UnitState_Moving.exit` cancels the in-flight repath request even though `MovementComponent.request_repath` would also cancel it on a subsequent call.** Contract §3.5 specifies states must own their own teardown. The next state may not be another Moving (could be Attacking, Constructing, or Idle), and those states won't re-issue a repath that would shadow ours. Explicit cancel in exit is cheap and matches the contract's intent. Implementation: `_movement._scheduler.cancel_repath(_movement._request_id)` then `_movement._request_id = -1` so MovementComponent's next `_sim_tick` doesn't poll the cancelled request.

- **`UnitState_Idle._sim_tick` writes `MeshInstance3D.scale` directly inside the sim tick.** Sim Contract §1.5 allows visual side-effects in `_process` (UI off-tick), but States are RefCounted and have no `_process`. The pulse runs from `_sim_tick` because that's the only hook a State has, and `MeshInstance3D.scale` is render-only — not a SimNode field, doesn't trigger the on-tick assert (we don't route through `_set_sim`), doesn't feed into combat math, pathfinding, or any sim-state read. This is the same carve-out MovementComponent uses for `Node3D.global_position` (Sim Contract §4.1). The pulse is driven by `SimClock.tick * SIM_DT` — deterministic, replay-safe, and removes a wall-clock divergence vector from headless determinism tests even though we don't strictly need determinism for visual decoration.

- **`UnitState_Moving.interrupt_level = COMBAT`, NOT `NEVER`.** Contract §2.1 spec: NONE = damage doesn't interrupt, COMBAT = damage interrupts, NEVER = damage cannot interrupt. "Non-combat movement" sits in the COMBAT bucket per the contract's own examples. Phase 2's combat system can flip this to NONE for "casual" movement (e.g., hero traveling between bases) if combat balance demands it; one-line edit. Player `replace_command` always wins regardless of `interrupt_level` (Contract §3.5).

- **What did not ship in wave 2** (intentionally out of scope per kickoff): Concrete additional states (Attacking, Gathering, Constructing, Casting, Dying) — Phase 2+ when their owning systems exist. GroupMoveController / formation movement — Phase 1 session 2 (planned row in §2 unchanged). MovementSystem phase coordinator — LATER item, see below. F3 state-machine debug overlay — concrete overlays land WITH their owning systems per kickoff doc rule; visual ID readout for selected unit lands when the selected-unit panel ships (Phase 1 session 2). The 6 deliverable boxes from the wave-2 brief: UnitState_Idle ✅, UnitState_Moving ✅, Wire Idle/Moving in Unit base ✅, 12-18 tests ✅ (13 shipped: 4 Idle + 8 Moving + 1 base-class registration test), ARCHITECTURE.md update ✅ (this entry), BUILD_LOG.md wave-2 entry ✅.

- **LATER items surfaced in wave 2:**
  1. **MovementSystem phase coordinator.** Currently Moving's `_sim_tick` drives `MovementComponent._sim_tick`. When 50+ units move simultaneously this becomes "every Moving state's _sim_tick calls a MovementComponent's _sim_tick" — fine for MVP but a phase coordinator that subscribes to `EventBus.sim_phase(&"movement", ...)` and iterates registered MovementComponents in one batch is the long-term shape (cache-friendlier, removes the per-state-instance drive call). Estimated 1 small wave; not blocking.
  2. **Per-unit current_command lifetime.** `Unit.current_command` is a Dictionary written by StateMachine and read by states. It outlives the dispatched Command (which is returned to the pool). When Phase 2's Attacking state lands, it'll need `current_command.payload.target_unit: Node` — a reference to a Node, which can become invalid mid-state. Either Attacking handles the validity check itself (preferred — same pattern as `is_instance_valid` checks elsewhere) or the dispatcher converts Node refs to unit_ids. Not a wave-2 problem; flagged for Phase 2 ai-engineer.

---

### v0.13.1 — Phase 1 Session 1 live-game fixes (2026-05-01) — lead

User-visible Definition of Done (kickoff §73, items 1–8) was confirmed green by the lead in the editor: 5 kargars spawn on the terrain plane; left-click selects (gold ring); right-click on terrain commands a move; the kargar walks the path; arrival returns to Idle pulse; click on empty terrain deselects. Three bugs blocked items 4–5 in the live game even though all 371 unit tests passed. Fixed in commit `c583d48`.

- **Unit FSM was never ticked in the live game.** `UnitState_Moving._sim_tick` polls the path scheduler and steps the position, but nothing in the live scene called `fsm.tick()` — tests called it directly, and the live game was waiting on the "MovementSystem phase coordinator" LATER item from v0.13.0. Fix: each `Unit` now subscribes to `EventBus.sim_phase` in `_ready` and calls `fsm.tick(SimClock.SIM_DT)` when `phase == &"movement"`. Symmetric `_exit_tree` disconnect. This is the same pattern `SpatialIndex` uses for `&"spatial_rebuild"`. **This is the single most important behavior to lock in via integration test (qa-engineer wave 3) — every unit-level test passed while the live game was silently broken.** When the proper MovementSystem coordinator ships, this is a 3-line removal: drop `_on_sim_phase`, drop the connect/disconnect, register the unit with the coordinator instead. See LATER item below.

- **Edge-pan moved opposite to camera-look.** Two issues stacked in `camera_controller.gd`. (a) `pan_by` did not rotate the screen-axis vector through the rig's basis; with the camera_rig.tscn yaw of +45°, screen-up did not follow camera-forward. Fixed by `world_pan = global_transform.basis * local_pan` (`is_inside_tree()`-guarded so headless test fixtures stay identity). (b) `compute_edge_pan_axis` used the opposite Y-sign convention from WASD: mouse-near-top produced `ax.y = -1` while pressing W produced `ax.y = +1`. The two paths cancelled into world directions opposite each other. Fixed by flipping edge-pan signs so mouse-near-top → `ax.y = +1` (matches WASD W). The original wave-1 tests asserted only the sign of `ax.y`, not the resulting world direction, so the bug slipped through. Tests updated; new comment documents the convention.

- **HUD labels swallowed clicks.** `Label` and `MarginContainer` default `mouse_filter` is `MOUSE_FILTER_STOP`, which silently absorbs mouse events that fall in the Control's rect. The `StatusLabel` (y=56–88), the HUD `MarginContainer` (top 48px), the `HBox`, and the four resource Labels were all eating clicks in their rects. Fix: `mouse_filter = 2` (IGNORE) on each. Defensive but correct — these Controls are decorative readouts, not interactive.

- **`DEBUG_LOG_CLICKS` flag added** in `click_handler.gd`. Default ON. Prints every left/right press, what the raycast hit, and what command (if any) was issued. This was the diagnostic that made bug #1 visible. Left ON for now so the next interactive testing session has the same visibility. Will be flipped off (or gated by `DebugOverlayManager`) once the path is trusted.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.13.1:**
  1. **MovementSystem phase coordinator** — promoted in priority. The transitional `Unit._on_sim_phase` works for the 5-unit Phase 1 case; at MVP scale (50–100 units) the per-unit signal-handler dispatch is fine, but the coordinator's deterministic `unit_id`-sorted iteration is the long-term shape. The Sim Contract §2 example for `MovementSystem` is the target signature. Estimated 1 small wave; not blocking.
  2. **Visual smoke test** — Phase 0 retro added a §9 rule about scene-level smoke tests; this set of bugs is the canonical "headless tests passed; live game broken" case the rule was written to catch. qa-engineer wave 3 is implementing the integration tests now. The lasting fix is a CI-runnable test that loads `main.tscn`, spawns a unit, drives ticks via `SimClock._test_advance`, and asserts the unit's `global_position` advances toward a commanded target. If that test had existed at the start of session 1, bug #1 would have been caught the moment Idle/Moving + Kargar shipped.

---

### v0.14.0 — Phase 1 Session 2 wave 1B (2026-05-03) — ai-engineer (GroupMoveController skeleton)

- **`GroupMoveController` lives in `scripts/movement/`, not `scripts/ai/`.** The kickoff brief authorized either location. `scripts/movement/` is a new directory; the rationale is that the controller is a pure dispatcher for the player's right-click — it touches no AI controller, no perception, no targeting heuristics. Keeping it next to (the future) `scripts/navigation/` mirrors how the directory map in §4 already groups path-related code, and leaves `scripts/ai/` exclusively for opponent-AI work (`DummyAIController`, `TuranController`). If a future AI-side use of group-move dispatch lands (e.g., AI panic-retreat for a squad), it imports the controller — same primitive, no relocation needed.

- **No `class_name` on the controller.** Same registry-race pattern as `MatchHarness` and the path-string `extends` pattern in `farr_system.gd` (§6 v0.4.0). Static methods on a preloaded script ref work identically with or without `class_name`; callers use `const _GMC := preload("..."); _GMC.dispatch_group_move(...)`. The kickoff brief explicitly authorized this choice; pre-empting the race rather than fighting it.

- **Offset radius 2.0 chosen for nav-snap survival.** `Constants.GROUP_MOVE_OFFSET_RADIUS = 2.0`, sized at 8× the navmesh `cell_size` (0.25 baked in `terrain.tscn`). The kickoff brief flagged this as the load-bearing live-game-broken-surface item — adjacent ring slots of 2.0 chord-length cannot collapse to the same nav-poly under `NavigationServer3D.map_get_path`'s snap-to-poly behavior. Headless tests use `MockPathScheduler` which returns straight-line targets without snapping, so a smaller radius would pass tests but fail in the live game. Documented in the constant's source comment and the controller header. (The constant itself was committed by balance-engineer in `42a2f9b` — wave 1B is a consumer.)

- **Concentric-ring algorithm (1 + 6 + 12 + 18…).** Index 0 sits at the click center; indices 1..6 fan out to a single ring of radius R at 60° spacing; indices 7..18 fall on a 2R ring at 30° spacing; etc. Phase 1's worker cap is 5, so all five units fit on ring 1 (one center + four-of-six ring slots actually used). The algorithm scales — a future 50-unit selection would distribute across 4 rings without any extra logic — but the simplest expression that meets the wave-1 requirement was the priority. Determinism is guaranteed by index-based trig (`cos(i × 60°)`, `sin(i × 60°)`); no `randf()`, no time, no scene state.

- **Single-unit fast path returns `target` verbatim.** Important behavioral detail: a 1-unit "group move" must be bitwise-identical to the existing single-click move. Skipping the offset math for `live.size() == 1` preserves that exactly — no float drift from a `cos(0) = 0.99999…` round-trip — and means the wave-2 click-handler wiring can route both single and multi selections through the controller without breaking the session-1 single-click test suite.

- **What did not ship in wave 1B (deferred to wave 2C):** Click-handler wiring. `click_handler.gd::process_right_click_hit` still calls `unit.replace_command(&"move", {target})` directly per unit. Wave 2C's job is to switch the multi-selection branch to `GroupMoveController.dispatch_group_move(selected, target)` while keeping the single-unit branch untouched (the controller's identity case makes this a 2-line change). The `📋 Planned` row in §2 is now `🟡 In progress`; flips to `✅ Built` when wave 2C lands.

- **What did not ship in wave 1B (out of scope per kickoff):** Facing/rotation (Phase 2). Formation-type selection (line, wedge, column — Phase 2). Reservation-based pathing where units claim individual destination tiles (Phase 3+ when buildings + spatial reservations exist). Off-navmesh target validation — kickoff brief explicitly said "each unit's `request_repath` will FAIL; that's the unit's problem, not yours." `UnitState_Moving`'s FAILED-path branch already handles this.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01):** see commit `9d54d79` body — three answers covering snap survival, formation feel/visual, and the lead's interactive smoke test.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.14.0:**
  1. **Wave 2C wiring** — `click_handler.gd::process_right_click_hit` 2-line swap.
  2. **Stress-test at higher unit counts** — Phase 2/3 army-scale selections.
  3. **Formation visualization for the F1 pathfinding overlay** — Phase 6 per CLAUDE.md.

---

### v0.14.1 — Phase 1 Session 2 wave 1A (2026-05-01) — ui-developer (Box / drag selection)

- **Two-file split: pure math vs. input handler.** `box_select_math.gd` (RefCounted, no class_name) holds `rect_from_corners`, `is_past_dead_zone`, `units_in_rect`. `box_select_handler.gd` (Node) holds the input-event flow, the projection sweep, and the SelectionManager wiring. The headless GUT runner can't reliably stand up a real `Camera3D + Viewport + scene tree` for `unproject_position`; splitting the math out lets the rectangle-vs-projected-point logic be unit-tested without the engine layer (16 math tests cover all four drag directions, dead-zone thresholding, on-screen filter, malformed-entry guards). The handler tests inject a `project_unit: Callable` into `box_select_units(rect, units, project_callable, shift)` so input flow + selection wiring is exercised without a Camera3D either (15 handler tests). The remaining live-game-broken-surface (real `Camera3D.unproject_position` against the live scene; mouse_filter behavior under real input) lands in the lead's interactive smoke test.

- **Coordination with `click_handler.gd` is one-direction (we forward; it never feeds us).** The kickoff said "do NOT modify selection_manager.gd or click_handler.gd core logic." `BoxSelectHandler` claims left-press first via `_unhandled_input` tree-order (sibling **after** `ClickHandler` in `main.tscn`, so `_unhandled_input` reaches it first under Godot's reverse-tree-order delivery). Always calls `set_input_as_handled()` on press AND release, so `ClickHandler` never sees the left button. On non-drag release (the click case), we re-raycast and forward the result to `ClickHandler.process_left_click_hit(hit)` — its existing public seam, which qa-engineer already test-covered (`test_click_handler.gd`). Right-click events still reach `ClickHandler` directly (we only intercept left-button presses). This preserves the "click_handler.gd untouched" contract: not one line edited; we depend on its public surface only.

- **Press-time Shift state, not release-time.** The handler captures `mb.shift_pressed` at press time and uses that value for the release-time selection mode. Real-world case: player hits Shift, presses, releases Shift mid-drag, then releases the mouse — the selection mode stays additive. This is the standard RTS behavior and matches StarCraft 2 / AoE2 muscle memory. Tested explicitly (`test_shift_state_uses_press_time_value`).

- **Drag overlay is a CanvasLayer with `mouse_filter = MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE` belt-and-braces.** The `.tscn` sets `mouse_filter = 2` on the Rect Control. The `_ready` of `drag_overlay.gd` AND `drag_overlay_rect.gd` re-asserts `mouse_filter = Control.MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE` at runtime as a defensive guard against future scene drift. Session 1's exact regression pattern (HUD labels at default `MOUSE_FILTER_STOP` swallowing clicks) is what we're inoculating against. The overlay CanvasLayer is `layer = 10` so it draws above the 3D viewport; the child Control is anchored full-rect (anchor_right/anchor_bottom = 1.0) so screen-space coords work without per-frame conversion.

- **Empty-rect drag deselects (no Shift) / preserves (Shift).** Drag on empty space with no Shift clears the selection — the documented "drag onto nothing = deselect" RTS convention. With Shift, prior selection is preserved (additive mode never destroys what's already there). Both paths covered by tests (`test_box_select_on_empty_rect_deselects_all_no_shift` and `test_box_select_on_empty_rect_with_shift_preserves_selection`).

- **Linear unit-iteration sweep, not SpatialIndex.** The handler walks `get_tree().current_scene` looking for unit-shaped Node3Ds (duck-typed: `unit_id` field, `team` field, `Node3D` instance). At Phase 1's worker cap of 5, the linear walk costs nothing; SpatialIndex would add an autoload dependency for no measurable benefit. The kickoff brief explicitly authorized either ("iterate the Units in the scene OR use SpatialIndex"). When the unit count grows past ~50 (Phase 2+), revisit. Filtered to `team == TEAM_IRAN` so the player only box-selects their own units; future enemy-target box-select for attack-move would relax this filter.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01 — refined):**
  1. *What state/behavior must work at runtime that no unit test exercises?* The drag overlay's `mouse_filter = MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE` (set in .tscn AND re-asserted in `_ready` of both `drag_overlay.gd` and `drag_overlay_rect.gd`). Real `Camera3D.unproject_position` per visible Iran unit on every release event (handler iterates `get_tree().current_scene` for unit-shaped Node3Ds with `team == TEAM_IRAN`). Coordination with `click_handler.gd`: BoxSelectHandler always claims the press; on non-drag release it re-raycasts and forwards via `ClickHandler.process_left_click_hit` — the only one-direction integration path that doesn't violate the "don't modify click_handler.gd" rule.
  2. *What can a headless test not detect that the lead would notice in the editor?* Visual: rectangle anchoring/transparency/stroke (1.0 alpha gold stroke @ 0.85, fill @ 0.20). Behavioral: drag-from-HUD-into-world (HUD's labels were set to MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE in session 1, so the press hits us — but if a future interactive HUD lands, its `_gui_input` should claim it before we see it). Drag in all 4 corner-directions (math tested; visual rect anchoring needs eyes). Quick-click with 1–3px jitter mistaken for drag (the 4px squared-distance threshold is the line; lead may want 6 or 8 if it feels twitchy on trackpad).
  3. *What's the minimum interactive smoke test that catches it?* Lead drags TL→BR across the 5 kargars: all 5 selected, gold rings appear. Lead drags BR→TL: same result (the math is direction-agnostic, but the visual rectangle should still anchor at the top-left of the dragged area). Lead Shift-drags a partial subset while 2 are already selected: only the new units are added; existing stay. Quick-click on one kargar with no drag: that one selects (single-click path through `ClickHandler.process_left_click_hit` still works). Click on empty terrain: deselect all. Drag onto empty space (no units inside the rect, no Shift): deselect all. Drag onto empty space with Shift: prior selection preserved.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.14.1:**
  1. **`SelectionManager.select_many(units)` to collapse the broadcast.** The current `_commit_selection` calls `deselect_all()` then `add_to_selection(u)` for each hit, which emits one `selection_changed` per unit. At Phase 1's scale this is invisible; at Phase 2's scale (large mixed-army selections) it's worth a single-broadcast API. Out of scope for wave 1A per the kickoff's "do NOT modify selection_manager.gd" rule. Flag for a follow-up wave when `SelectionManager` next gets touched.
  2. **Formation-shape selection feedback.** When the player drags a rect, the units inside light up immediately on release; there's no "drag-preview" highlight (units the rect would catch are NOT visually flagged until release). Standard RTS UX has a soft hover-style highlight while the rect is active. Phase 2+ when the visual polish budget opens up.
  3. **Empty-rect drag interaction with right-click cancellation.** Right-click during an active drag currently doesn't cancel the drag (the drag completes on left-release per the captured shift state). RTS convention is "right-click during marquee = cancel." Tracked but not blocking — wait for lead feel-test feedback before changing.

---

### v0.14.2 — Phase 1 Session 2 wave 2C (2026-05-04) — ai-engineer (GroupMoveController wire-up)

- **The 2-line behavioral swap landed.** `click_handler.gd::process_right_click_hit` previously walked the selected-units array and called `u.call(&"replace_command", Constants.COMMAND_MOVE, payload)` once per unit with the same target. Wave 2C replaces that loop with `_GroupMove.dispatch_group_move(sel, target)` (preloaded at file scope as `const _GroupMove := preload("res://scripts/movement/group_move_controller.gd")`). Single-unit selections still get the click point verbatim (the controller's identity fast path); multi-unit selections fan out across the deterministic ring in `Constants.GROUP_MOVE_OFFSET_RADIUS`. The `kickoff §137` "do NOT modify click_handler.gd core logic" rule was the wave-1 contract; wave 2C is the explicitly authorized exception per the wave-2C brief, and the change is contained to the multi-selection branch only — the raycast, no-selection short-circuit, hit-on-unit short-circuit, and DEBUG_LOG_CLICKS instrumentation are untouched.

- **Why both branches go through the controller (not "single-unit keeps the old loop").** The kickoff explicitly authorized this — the controller's `live.size() == 1` fast path returns `target` verbatim with no offset math, so a single-click move is bitwise-identical to the pre-wire-up behavior. Routing both through one dispatcher means future changes to the move-dispatch path (e.g., adding a queueing mode, a logging hook, an Attack-Move path) edit one place, not two. The session-1 single-click test suite still passes because the observable behavior didn't change: 1 selected unit → 1 `replace_command` call with `{&"target": click_point}`.

- **`Unit.has_method(&"replace_command")` defensive check dropped.** The previous loop did `if u.has_method(&"replace_command"): u.call(...)`. The controller calls `live[i].replace_command(...)` directly without a method-existence check — it relies on `is_instance_valid()` filtering only. This is safe because `SelectionManager` only stores Unit-shaped objects (its `select` API itself uses the `command_queue` + `replace_command` duck-type via `_is_unit_shaped`), and `is_instance_valid()` covers freed entries. The defensive check was load-bearing for a hypothetical future where someone shoves a non-Unit into the selection — that's a contract violation, not a runtime case worth a per-call check. If this assumption ever flips, `SelectionManager` is the right place to enforce it (one gate, not every dispatch site).

- **Three new tests in `test_click_handler.gd` (+3, total 472 → was 469 in HEAD).** `test_right_click_multi_selection_distributes_targets` (TDD-red on the unwired baseline; verifies that 3 selected units produce ≥2 pairs of distinct targets — the "no piling" guarantee). `test_right_click_multi_selection_targets_within_radius` (each dispatched target lies within `GROUP_MOVE_OFFSET_RADIUS` of the click on the XZ plane; Y is preserved verbatim). `test_right_click_single_selection_target_unchanged` (regression guard for the session-1 single-click suite — the controller's identity path keeps single-selection bitwise-identical). The existing `test_right_click_pushes_command_to_every_selected_unit` test still passes (the controller dispatches one `replace_command` per live unit; observable end state matches).

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01 — refined):**
  1. *What state/behavior must work at runtime that no unit test exercises?* The wire-up is exercised by every right-click in the live game — that part headless tests cover via `process_right_click_hit(hit)` synthetic dispatch. What they cannot reach: the chain `box_select_handler.gd → SelectionManager.add_to_selection (×N) → click_handler.gd._unhandled_input(MOUSE_BUTTON_RIGHT) → raycast → GroupMoveController.dispatch_group_move → unit.replace_command → StateMachine.transition_to_next → UnitState_Moving.enter() → MovementComponent.request_repath`. `NavigationAgentPathScheduler` (production scheduler) snaps each offset target to the nearest navmesh poly; `MockPathScheduler` does not. R = 2.0 (8× the 0.25 navmesh `cell_size`) keeps adjacent ring slots distinct against snap-to-poly per wave 1B's analysis. With box-select shipping in wave 1A, this wave-2C wiring is the **first time multi-unit movement actually exercises the production navmesh path with real offset targets** — until now there was no UI path to put 2+ kargars in the selection.
  2. *What can a headless test not detect that the lead would notice in the editor?* The visible spread of 5 kargars arriving at distinct positions vs. piling up — a feel question that passes tests both ways. The mid-move redirect behavior (right-click while units are still moving): does the second dispatch cleanly cancel the first repath and re-issue with new ring offsets, or does it stutter? Whether a quick double-right-click on nearby points feels like "go there, then adjust" or jitters. Whether the formation rotation looks right (it shouldn't — facing/rotation is Phase 2; if the lead sees rotation here, that's a regression in `UnitState_Moving`).
  3. *What's the minimum interactive smoke test that catches it?* Lead box-selects all 5 kargars (now possible with wave 1A's marquee), right-clicks a far point: all 5 walk, no piling, ring is visibly distributed. Lead right-clicks again mid-motion: clean redirect, all 5 still distributed at the new target. Lead right-clicks near a navmesh edge: the off-navmesh-ring-slots fail individually via `request_repath` FAILED, drop back to Idle (per `UnitState_Moving`'s FAILED branch); other slots still walk. This is the interactive test wave-1B flagged as "testable from the keyboard after wave 2C wiring" — wave 2C is what makes it real.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.14.2:**
  1. **Shift-queue formation moves.** The controller has a sister primitive `append_command` (per State Machine Contract §2.5) that would drive Shift-queue waypoint moves. Right-click currently hardcodes `replace_command` (right-click semantics, not Shift-queue). When the keybinding wave lands Shift+right-click, the click handler can branch on `mb.shift_pressed` and dispatch through a `dispatch_group_move_append` variant. Out of scope for 2C per the kickoff.
  2. **Right-click on enemy unit / friendly unit.** Currently no-op (Phase 2's attack-move and follow/guard land here). The controller's `dispatch_group_move` is target-agnostic — it dispatches `&"move"` only. Attack-move will need a parallel `dispatch_group_attack_move` that dispatches `&"attack_move"` (or a kind argument on the existing dispatcher). Phase 2.
  3. **Stress-test mid-move-redirect at higher unit counts.** With 5 kargars the mid-move-redirect is fine; at 50+ units (Phase 2/3 army-scale selections) the per-tick MovementComponent repath cancel + reissue cost may be measurable. Profile when army-scale selections actually exist; not blocking now.

---

### v0.14.3 — Phase 1 Session 2 wave 2B (2026-05-04) — ui-developer (Selected-unit panel)

- **No `unit_health_changed` signal exists; HP polled in `_process` against the displayed unit.** The kickoff brief said "subscribe to `EventBus.unit_health_changed` (verify exact signal name)" — verification revealed the signal does not exist. The only HealthComponent emission is `EventBus.unit_health_zero(unit_id)`, fired once at hp=0 as the StateMachine death-preempt trigger (per State Machine Contract §4.2). Adding a per-tick `unit_health_changed` signal would emit write-shaped EventBus signals from `_sim_tick` for every damaged unit on every tick — wasteful when 99% of the time no UI consumer cares, and a write-shaped signal in tick state needs L2-allowlist plumbing. Polling one displayed unit each `_process` frame is O(1), stays off-tick (Sim Contract §1.5: UI reads sim state freely off-tick), and matches the resource_hud.gd pattern for Coin/Grain/Pop reads. When CombatSystem ships in Phase 2 and damage numbers / floating-text feedback need on-change precision, that's the right time to add a targeted signal. Until then: poll.

- **`refresh_displayed_unit()` not `apply_*` — lint rule L1.** `tools/lint_simulation.sh` rule L1 forbids any `apply_*` method in a file that defines `_process` (the convention "`apply_*` means sim-side mutator," documented in §6 v0.6.0). Selected-unit panel runs `_process` for HP polling, so the public refresh seam is `refresh_displayed_unit()`. Same precedent the camera controller set with `pan_by` / `zoom_by`. The naming is the lint signal that this is UI-side state, not sim-side.

- **Three sub-layouts toggled by `visible_state` tag, not by parent visibility alone.** The panel exposes `visible_state: StringName` (`&"empty"` / `&"single"` / `&"multi"`) so tests assert on the stable identifier rather than walking nested visibility properties. Visual tweaks (collapsing EmptyLayout into a styled root background, adding a `&"multi_overflow"` state for >12 selections) become refactor-safe — the test contract is the tag, not the node tree.

- **Multi-select icon Buttons use a child ColorRect swatch, not a theme override.** Godot's `Button` node has no built-in tint property; the standard placeholder approach is a child `ColorRect` filling the button's rect. The button itself is `MOUSE_FILTER_STOP` (catches the click), the swatch is `MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE` (lets the click reach the button). Tooltip carries the unit's translated type name. Each Button's `pressed` signal is `.bind(unit_id)` at creation time, so the click resolves to the correct unit even if the icon list reshuffles between render and click — defensive `is_instance_valid` walk through `SelectionManager.selected_units` further filters freed units at click time. `_MAX_ICONS = 12` (3 rows of 4) caps panel growth; overflow rendering is a Phase 2 polish concern.

- **Twelve new tests in `test_selected_unit_panel.gd` (+12).** Scene loads, root is CanvasLayer; mouse_filter discipline (no non-button container is MOUSE_FILTER_STOP — recursive walk finds offenders); empty / single / multi states; HP bar reflects health; type label uses `tr()`; multi-selection icon click narrows via `select_only`; freed-unit icon click is safe no-op; freed displayed unit transitions panel out of `&"single"` state; translation keys (UI_PANEL_NO_SELECTION, UI_PANEL_HP, UI_PANEL_ABILITIES, UNIT_KARGAR) all resolve to English under en locale. Headless GUT: all 12 pass alongside the existing 472 (post wave-2A/2B/2C aggregation; 484 total at this commit before the parallel double-click and control-groups waves land their own tests).

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01 — refined):**
  1. *What state/behavior must work at runtime that no unit test exercises?* The signal-driven re-render cycle when selection changes mid-frame (e.g., box-select releases → SelectionManager broadcasts → panel rebuilds icon grid → player clicks an icon → SelectionManager broadcasts again → panel rebuilds to single-state). Headless tests dispatch each step in isolation; the live game stacks them within a single frame's input + render cycle. Icon-button signal connections survive the rebuild because we `queue_free` old buttons (deferred — the click that triggered the narrow can complete before the buttons are gone). The `_process` HP poll on a freed unit (race between "unit dies" and "panel re-renders to empty") — the `is_instance_valid` guard in `refresh_displayed_unit` falls back to `_render_empty()` defensively. None of these races are deterministic; only live runtime exercises the timing.
  2. *What can a headless test not detect that the lead would notice in the editor?* Visual layout — does the 250×120 panel feel right at 1280×720? Does it overlap with anything (control-group HUD bar, Phase 2+)? Does the bottom-left anchor survive at 1920×1080 / 2560×1440 without scaling weirdly? Does the placeholder grey-rect aesthetic clash visually with the FarrGauge's gold-ivory palette? Multi-select icon grid layout — at 12 icons (3 rows of 4), is the panel still legible? Are the icon swatches large enough to distinguish faction colors? Does clicking the icon feel responsive (sub-50ms perceived) or laggy? The HP bar fill ColorRect — does the proportional width update look smooth as HP drops, or does it pop discretely (we resize each `_process` so it should be smooth, but the ColorRect's anchor preset may snap at certain ratios)? None of this is observable from `visible_state` / `hp_ratio` reads.
  3. *What's the minimum interactive smoke test that catches it?* Lead boots, sees nothing in the panel ("No selection" centered). Lead clicks a kargar: panel shows portrait (sandy-brown), "Kargar" label, full HP bar, 4 grey ability rects. Lead box-selects all 5: panel shows 5 sandy-brown icon swatches in a row (still under 12 cap). Lead clicks the 3rd icon: selection narrows to that one kargar; panel transitions back to single-layout for that specific unit. Lead clicks empty terrain: panel returns to "No selection" centered. Lead's 30-second loop. If the panel covers up the FarrGauge, ResourceHUD, or the kargars themselves at 1280×720, that's the LATER candidate.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.14.3:**
  1. **HP-change targeted signal when CombatSystem ships (Phase 2).** Polling is fine for one displayed unit at MVP; when the panel needs to render damage flashes or floating numbers ("-12 HP"), a `unit_health_changed(unit_id, hp_after, max_hp, source_unit_id)` signal becomes load-bearing. Add to EventBus alongside `unit_died` and `damage_dealt`; emit from `HealthComponent.take_damage` (already on-tick). The poll path stays as the fallback for non-displayed units' HP renders.
  2. **Multi-select overflow rendering.** Currently caps at 12 icons silently. Beyond 12, render the first 12 plus a "+N more" tag — Phase 2 polish; not load-bearing while Phase 1 caps at 5 kargars.
  3. **Subgroup management beyond icon-narrows-to-one.** Modern RTS panels let players ctrl-click an icon to remove that one unit, or shift-click to select-only-that-type within the multi-selection. Out of scope per kickoff §2 (6); pencil in for Phase 2 selection polish if lead-test feedback flags it.
  4. **Real portraits + real ability buttons.** Placeholder rects per CLAUDE.md until the design chat green-lights art. When portraits land, the `_portrait` ColorRect becomes a `TextureRect` reading from a `unit_portrait_path` field on UnitStats; ability rects become `Button`s wired to the unit's `ability_set` (Phase 2 with Rostam's hero abilities).
  5. **Font-size i18n.** The panel's labels use `ThemeDB.fallback_font` at default sizes. When the Persian column lands at Tier 2, the Latin → Persian script change may need a different font face and a different size to feel right — that's a theme override on the panel root, not a code change. Documented but no work needed pre-fa.

---

### v0.14.5 — Phase 1 Session 2 wave 3 (2026-05-01) — qa-engineer (Integration tests: session-2 flows)

- **37 new integration tests across 5 files; test count 498 → 535.** Coverage: box/drag selection (public test seams, no real Camera3D), control group bind/recall/center round-trip (stub CameraController injected via `set_camera_target`), group-move pile-prevention (5-unit dispatch → ≥4 distinct XZ positions within ε=0.5), Farr gauge listener (target_farr + color_band on `farr_changed` signal, off-tick per Sim Contract §1.5), selected-unit panel content (empty/single/multi states, death, icon click, MOUSE_FILTER_STOP regression guard), and a cross-feature smoke test. 3 pre-existing PENDING unchanged (FarrSystem fallback, navmesh ×2).

- **`add_child_autofree` BEFORE `global_position` assignment is load-bearing.** `Node3D.global_transform` asserts `is_inside_tree()`. Setting `global_position` before adding the node to the scene tree silently returns `Transform3D()` and prints "Condition '!is_inside_tree()' is true." — the unit appears at origin regardless of the value written. All `_spawn_kargar` helpers follow the pattern: `add_child_autofree(u)` first, then `u.global_position = pos`. This is the correct order for all Node3D instantiation in tests.

- **Smoke test step-5 (narrow single-select) uses the unit's actual post-movement screen position.** Units move to formation positions around (20,0,20) in step 2; their exact positions depend on ring offsets. Hardcoding screen coordinates based on original spawn positions selected 0 units. Fix: call `_project_unit(800, 600).call(target_unit)["screen_pos"]` against the first live unit's CURRENT `global_position`, then build a tight 1.2×1.2 Rect2 centered there. The 1.2×1.2 size guarantees exactly 1 unit at the 10:1 projection scale since ring slots are ≥2.0 world units apart (≥20 screen pixels).

- **Farr gauge signal tests are off-tick per Sim Contract §1.5.** `EventBus.farr_changed` is emitted directly in tests without advancing `SimClock`. `gauge.target_farr` and `gauge.color_band` are read immediately after the emit — both update synchronously in the gauge's signal handler. No `await get_tree().process_frame` needed (and none used) — adding an `await` would allow deferred UI updates that mask synchronous-update bugs.

- **HP partial health written via `hp_x100` backing field, not `hp`.** `HealthComponent.hp` is a read-only getter computed from `hp_x100`; `hc.set(&"hp", value)` silently does nothing in GDScript. Tests write `hc.set(&"hp_x100", max_x100 / 2)` directly. The `max_hp_x100` field is also read via `hc.get(&"max_hp_x100")` for safety (avoids hardcoding the kargar's max_hp value in the test itself).

- **MOUSE_FILTER_STOP regression guard in panel tests.** `test_panel_root_does_not_swallow_clicks_via_mouse_filter` recursively walks all `Control` nodes under the panel and asserts that none have `MOUSE_FILTER_STOP` unless they are a `Button`. This locks in the session-1 fix (click-eating HUD bug) so it cannot regress if panel layout changes. The Button carve-out is correct — icon Buttons legitimately stop clicks.

- **main.tscn spot-check confirms DoubleClickSelect + SelectedUnitPanel coexistence.** Both wave-2A and wave-2B nodes were committed separately. Loading `main.tscn` as a `PackedScene` and calling `get_node_or_null` + `has_method` duck-typing confirms neither clobbered the other. This test is the Experiment 01 live-game-broken-surface answer: had it existed in session 1, it would have caught the cross-agent stomp scenario.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01 — wave 3):**
  1. *What state/behavior must work at runtime that no integration test exercises?* Real `Camera3D.unproject_position` path — all tests inject a linear projection callable. Actual NavMesh snap behavior in group-move — tests use MockPathScheduler which returns straight-line paths; navmesh snap-to-poly may collapse ring offsets in live play (the production-scheduler integration test is marked PENDING when no baked navmesh exists). EventBus signal delivery order — tests emit `farr_changed` directly; in live play SimClock drives `apply_farr_change` inside a tick, which may interleave with other `sim_phase` subscribers.
  2. *What can a headless test not detect?* Panel rendering at different viewport sizes (all tests assume 800×600 projection). Tween animation of the Farr gauge (tests read `target_farr` and `color_band`; the tween's intermediate steps are UI-only and headless-invisible). Whether the smoke test's 120-tick budget is tight enough at slower machines (tick rate is deterministic but total wall time varies).
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test:* Lead boxes 5 kargars → right-click move → watch them spread without piling → bind Ctrl+1 → click empty space → press 1 → same 5 reselected → panel shows STATE_MULTI with 5 icons → click one icon → panel shows STATE_SINGLE. Farr gauge changes color when Farr drops below 15. Both SelectedUnitPanel and DoubleClickSelect are present and functional.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.14.5:**
  1. **Production-scheduler pile-prevention test.** The group-move integration tests use MockPathScheduler. The PENDING test `test_5_units_move_to_distinct_positions_via_production_scheduler` (in `test_session_2_group_move.gd`) should be enabled once a baked navmesh is available in the test scene. This is the last gap in the live-game-broken-surface coverage for group move.
  2. **Farr gauge tween intermediate color-band test.** Currently tests read `color_band` after the signal; the tween may display the wrong band during animation if the `color_band` update in `_process` step is missed. A tween-step spy (or faster tween duration in tests) could cover this. Defer to Phase 2 visual polish.
  3. **Selected-unit panel HP polling frequency.** Panel polls `get_health().hp` every `_process` frame. With 5 units selected and switching between single-display, this is O(1) per frame — fine at Phase 1. At Phase 2+ when there are 50+ units and combat damage is continuous, the HP delta on the displayed unit will be imperceptible. Defer until combat ships.

### v0.15.0 — Phase 2 Session 1 wave 1C (2026-05-01) — balance-engineer (BalanceData combat fields)

- **Three new `UnitStats` fields for Phase 2 combat (`attack_damage_x100`, `attack_speed_per_sec`).** `attack_range` was already present from Phase 0. The two new fields follow the Sim Contract §1.6 fixed-point convention: `attack_damage_x100` stores damage × 100 as `int` to eliminate float drift at 30 Hz tick rates. `attack_speed_per_sec` is a `float` since it drives a cooldown denominator, not a tick counter. The legacy `damage: float` and `attack_speed_ticks: int` fields are retained — existing kargar/piyade/kamandar entries populated them and other agents' code may read them. Phase 2 `CombatComponent` reads the new fields only.

- **Kargar `attack_damage_x100 = 0` is the "cannot attack" sentinel.** `attack_range` set to `0.0` (was `1.0` — was an oversight in Phase 0; 1.0 implied it could enter melee range). `CombatComponent` will skip the attack tick when `attack_damage_x100 == 0`.

- **`turan_piyade` entry added to balance.tres.** Mirrors Iran `piyade` exactly — `max_hp=100`, `attack_damage_x100=1000`, `attack_speed_per_sec=1.0`, `attack_range=1.5`. RPS effectiveness differentiating Turan vs Iran units ships in Phase 2 session 2. A TODO comment in the sub-resource marks the gap.

- **`Constants.ENGAGE_RADIUS = 4.0` added under new `# === COMBAT ===` section.** Used by `UnitState_AttackMove` to decide when to break from move and engage. Sized at ~2.7× max melee range (1.5). Tunable without code change when Kamandar (ranged, range 8.0) ships.

- **`validate_hard()` extended for new fields.** Three new hard invariants: `attack_damage_x100 >= 0`, `attack_speed_per_sec > 0` (divide-by-zero guard in cooldown calc), `attack_range >= 0`. `validate_soft()` warns on suspiciously high values (>10000 damage, >100 speed, >50 range).

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.15.0:**
  1. **Kamandar combat fields unpopulated.** Kamandar in balance.tres uses GDScript defaults (`attack_damage_x100 = 0`, `attack_speed_per_sec = 1.0`). It will appear as a non-attacking unit until Phase 2 session 2 populates its combat fields alongside the full RPS matrix.
  2. **`piyade.max_hp` changed from 120.0 → 100.0.** Phase 0 value was 120; session-1 kickoff brief specifies 100 (1.7× Kargar's 60). The prior 120 value was also a "starting point to be tuned" per §0. Any test asserting `max_hp == 120` should be updated; currently `test_balance_data.gd` asserts 100.

---

### v0.16.0 — Phase 2 Session 1 wave 1A (2026-05-01) — gameplay-systems (CombatComponent + HealthComponent death-emit expansion)

- **`CombatComponent` ships at `scripts/units/components/combat_component.gd`.** Path-string SimNode base (matches HealthComponent / MovementComponent / FarrSystem registry-race pattern). Holds `attack_damage_x100: int`, `attack_speed_per_sec: float`, `attack_range: float` (read from BalanceData by Unit `_apply_balance_data_defaults`); internal `_target_unit_id: int = -1` and `_attack_cooldown_ticks: int = 0` (both written via `_set_sim`). `set_target(uid)` is the public command interface; `_sim_tick` runs cooldown decrement → target resolution → XZ-range check → fire (calls `target.get_health().take_damage_x100`). Production target lookup walks the scene tree O(N) per missed lookup; tests inject a closure (mirrors MovementComponent's `_scheduler` pattern from Sim Contract §4.1). Wired into `unit.tscn` as a sibling of MovementComponent; Unit `_apply_balance_data_defaults` reads the three combat fields with defensive type checks.

- **`HealthComponent` extended with the fixed-point hot path + cause-aware unit_died emit.** New `take_damage_x100(amount_x100: int, source: Node = null, cause: StringName = &"unspecified")` is the integer-only chokepoint CombatComponent calls per attack tick — no float→fixed-point round-trip. Both float `take_damage` and fixed-point `take_damage_x100` converge in private `_apply_damage_x100(amount_x100, source, cause)`. New field `last_death_position: Vector3` captured from parent Node3D's `global_position` BEFORE either signal fires; Phase 5 Yadgar building reads off the listener-side `unit_died` payload (`position` field) so it never calls back into a possibly-freed component. `killer_unit_id` resolved duck-typed from `source.unit_id` (`-1` sentinel when source is null or has no `unit_id`).

- **Death-emit listener-order discipline (cb95d09 lesson).** `EventBus.unit_health_zero(unit_id)` fires FIRST (StateMachine death-preempt per State Machine Contract §4.2), then `EventBus.unit_died(unit_id, killer_unit_id, cause, position)` (broader telemetry / Farr-drain channel). The `_zero_emitted` latch is set via `_set_sim` BEFORE either emit so a re-entrant listener that synchronously damages the same component can't recurse through the death path. Single latch covers both signals — over-kill ticks emit neither.

- **`EventBus.unit_died` signal added** with `(unit_id: int, killer_unit_id: int, cause: StringName, position: Vector3)` payload. Forwarder arm added to `_make_forwarder` for the four-arg signature; `_SINK_SIGNALS` extended so MatchLogger (Phase 6) sinks it automatically. Comment block above the declaration warns listeners against synchronous cross-listener mutation.

- **Why fixed-point damage instead of pure float?** Per Sim Contract §1.6, gameplay state that accumulates over a match (Farr, hp) stores as fixed-point int to eliminate IEEE-754 platform divergence over thousands of ticks. CombatComponent's `attack_damage_x100` matches `HealthComponent.hp_x100` so the subtraction is `hp_x100 -= attack_damage_x100` with zero rounding. The float `take_damage` wrapper still exists for legacy callers (Farr drain pathways, tests) — both wrappers funnel through `_apply_damage_x100` so the death-emit discipline is identical regardless of entry point.

- **`set_target` resets cooldown to 0 on engagement.** First tick after `set_target(uid)` fires immediately (single-tick attack on engagement, matches RTS convention). The shipped tests verify `_attack_cooldown_ticks == 30` after the swing at 1.0 atk/s on 30 Hz, and `== 15` at 2.0 atk/s — pinning the cooldown formula `roundi(SimClock.SIM_HZ / attack_speed_per_sec)` directly.

- **CombatComponent target lookup is `target_lookup_callable` injection — production wires a tree-walk fallback.** Production callable walks `get_tree().root` looking for a Node3D with matching `unit_id` (O(N) per missed lookup, acceptable at session-1 scale ≤15 units). Tests assign a closure over fixture Node3Ds — same injection seam shape as MovementComponent's `_scheduler`. The `is_instance_valid` defense in `_resolve_target` is what makes "freed target safe-clear" work: if the unit was queue_freed mid-engagement, the next `_sim_tick` lookup sees null, `_target_unit_id` is reset to -1 via `_set_sim`, no fire, no crash.

- **Forward-resolved task #139's `has_method(&"take_damage_x100")` guard.** When CombatComponent shipped earlier in the wave, `take_damage_x100` didn't yet exist on HealthComponent — the implementation guarded with `has_method` so it would no-op gracefully. With wave 1A complete, the chokepoint is real and the guard is now always-true; can be removed in a future cleanup pass without behavior change.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.16.0:**
  1. **`UnitRegistry` autoload (id → ref dict).** Production target lookup is O(N) tree-walk per missed lookup. Acceptable at session-1's 15-unit cap; needs replacement when N>~100 (mid-Phase 3 economy + Phase 6 AI). Closes target lookup to O(1).
  2. **CombatSystem phase coordinator.** Same shape as the future MovementSystem coordinator (§6 v0.10.0). Currently UnitState_Attacking drives CombatComponent's `_sim_tick` directly via Unit's StateMachine tick path. When the coordinator lands, it iterates registered CombatComponents during the `combat` phase and calls their `_sim_tick`; UnitState_Attacking drops the explicit drive call. One-line refactor.
  3. **Cleanup of CombatComponent's `has_method(&"take_damage_x100")` guard.** Now always-true; can be removed without behavior change in a future cleanup pass.
  4. **Float `take_damage` legacy path could be deprecated.** All Phase 2+ damage flows through `take_damage_x100`; the float wrapper exists only for pre-Phase-2 callers and tests. If those migrate, the float path can shrink to a thin convenience that round-trips to fixed-point — or be removed entirely.

---

### v0.16.1 — Phase 2 Session 1 wave 1B (2026-05-01) — ai-engineer (UnitState_Attacking)

- **`UnitState_Attacking` is the third concrete UnitState — same path-string base, same registry-race dodge.** Ships at `scripts/units/states/unit_state_attacking.gd` extending the path-string `unit_state.gd` base alongside Idle and Moving. id=`&"attacking"`, priority=20 (above Moving's 10 — when both are valid same tick, Attacking takes precedence; relevant for the future attack-move state's engage transition), interrupt_level=NEVER. Per State Machine Contract §3.5, `INTERRUPT_NEVER` blocks damage-driven preemption only — player `replace_command` and death always win. Damage during Attacking flows through `EventBus.unit_health_zero` → `StateMachine._on_unit_health_zero` → force-transition to Dying (Contract §4); the NEVER level concerns `interrupt_level`-based interrupts, not death. Unit base class `_ready` registers Attacking idempotently after Idle and Moving (gated by `not fsm._states.has(&"attacking")`), matching the wave-2 default-pair pattern.

- **Target lookup is a scene-tree walk, not a SpatialIndex query.** `_find_unit_by_id` recursively walks `get_tree().current_scene` (with a `tree.root` fallback for tests where current_scene is null) matching `unit_id == target_id`. SpatialIndex isn't appropriate here — it returns agents within a radius, not by id. Phase 2's 15-unit cap (5 Kargar + 5 Iran Piyade + 5 Turan Piyade) makes the linear walk free; at 100+ units (Phase 2 session 2 + multi-unit-roster expansion) this becomes O(N) per attack-state entry. **LATER**: a `UnitRegistry` autoload (id → ref Dictionary), populated by `Unit._ready` and depopulated by `Unit._exit_tree`, closes target lookup to O(1). This LATER item is now duplicated across wave 1A (CombatComponent's per-fire target lookup) and wave 1B (Attacking's per-engagement target lookup); both consumers benefit from the same primitive.

- **CombatComponent surface is read defensively.** `enter()` calls `ctx.has_method(&"get_combat")` then `ctx.get_combat()`; `_sim_tick` reads `_combat.attack_range` via `&"attack_range" in _combat` and calls `_combat.set_target(uid)` via `_combat.has_method(&"set_target")`. This wave's commit landed bundled with wave 1A in `81cf42a`, but the defensive guards remain useful: a future unit type that has no CombatComponent (e.g., a pure-utility worker that never engages) still gets sensible Attacking-state behavior — out-of-range targets drive `MovementComponent.request_repath`, in-range targets `push_warning` and no-op on the combat side. Default `attack_range=1.5` (matches the kickoff §2 deliverable 5 Piyade default) keeps the no-CombatComponent path producing "walk into melee then stop" behavior for live-test exploration.

- **Out-of-range movement strategy: option (b) — drive `request_repath` directly each tick.** The kickoff §2 deliverable 2 brief flagged two options: (a) re-issue a Move command via the queue (would compete with future commands) or (b) drive `MovementComponent.request_repath(target.global_position)` directly without going through the command queue, and let the unit walk while the state stays in Attacking. We chose (b) — cleaner, the state owns movement directly, and the queue stays clean for Shift-queued follow-up commands. The per-tick re-request cost (the scheduler cancels the prior in-flight request internally on each new request, so it's safe but not free) is fine for Phase 2's 15-unit cap. **LATER**: throttle to every-N-ticks OR introduce a stale-distance threshold (only re-issue when the target has moved more than X units since the last request) when N>50.

- **`exit()` cleanup matches `UnitState_Moving.exit()`'s shape.** Two defensive cleanups: `combat.set_target(-1)` so CombatComponent doesn't keep firing at the prior target after the state ends (deliberate symmetry with `enter()` setting the target); cancel any in-flight repath via `_scheduler.cancel_repath(_request_id)` followed by `_request_id = -1` so MovementComponent doesn't poll a cancelled request. Per Contract §3.5 the typical exit cause is `replace_command` from the player or death-preempt — both demand a clean teardown.

- **No signal emissions from inside the state.** Per the kickoff §2 deliverable 2 brief's Pitfall #4 (`cb95d09` re-entrant signal recursion lesson): combat-side signals (`unit_died`, `damage_dealt` when it ships) are emitted by `HealthComponent` / `CombatComponent`, not by the state. Reading `SelectionManager` / scene tree mid-tick is fine (read-shaped); emitting any `EventBus.X_changed` from a state's tick would expose the same `cb95d09` class of bug if a listener mutated the same state-holder. Verified by inspection — no `EventBus.<signal>.emit(...)` calls in `unit_state_attacking.gd`.

- **Two-tick-per-test pattern (drain pending → enter, then _sim_tick).** StateMachine.tick runs `current._sim_tick(dt, ctx)` first, THEN drains `_pending_id`. So `transition_to(&"attacking")` followed by one `tick()` call lands the FSM in Attacking (Idle's _sim_tick is empty; the swap calls Attacking's `enter()`). A SECOND tick is required for `Attacking._sim_tick` to actually run. Tests that exercise `_sim_tick` behavior (request_repath, set_target, repath cancellation) call `_tick_attacker()` twice; tests that exercise enter() behavior alone call it once. Contrast with Moving's tests where `enter()` itself issues request_repath, so one tick suffices — Attacking's `enter()` only caches refs, all behavior lives in `_sim_tick`. Documented as a test idiom for future combat-state additions.

- **Test stub (`_StubCombat extends Node`) mirrors the production CombatComponent surface.** `attack_range: float`, `set_target(unit_id: int)`, plus a test-only `last_set_target: int` field for assertion. The fixture `_spawn_unit_with_stub_combat` instantiates `unit.tscn`, removes any existing `CombatComponent` child (defensive against gameplay-systems' wave 1A wiring landing first — which it has), attaches the stub as a child named `CombatComponent` so `get_node_or_null(^"CombatComponent")` resolves to the stub, and writes `_combat_component = stub` to override the @onready cache. Both wave-1A's tests (using the real CombatComponent) and this wave's tests (using the stub) coexist; the stub lives only inside this test file.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01 — refined):**
  1. *State/behavior that must work at runtime that no unit test exercises:* The Moving → Attacking → Moving redirection when a target moves out of range mid-combat. Tests fix the target's position; live game has the target retreating or other units shoving it (Phase 3 collision-push). The `_sim_tick` re-issues `request_repath` each tick to the target's CURRENT position — a per-tick cost measurable in the lead's smoke test if 5 attackers chase 5 retreating targets across the map. The scene-tree walk for target lookup runs only on `enter()`, not per tick — that's the savings; the unit-by-id lookup happens once per attack engagement.
  2. *What headless tests cannot detect that the lead would notice in editor:* Whether the unit "snaps" to face the target (no rotation logic — Phase 5 polish; if rotation appears, that's a regression elsewhere). Whether interrupting an attack via `replace_command` (player reissues a Move command mid-fight) feels responsive — `INTERRUPT_NEVER` blocks damage interrupts only, not player commands; this should feel instant. Whether attack-on-death (target dies mid-tick) jitters or transitions cleanly — the `is_instance_valid` check on the cached target ref guards against the freed-mid-tick case, but the lead may notice a frame of "swing into nothing" before the state ends.
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test (post-wave-2B click_handler wiring + post-wave-1A CombatComponent):* Lead selects an Iran Piyade, right-clicks a Turan Piyade across the map → unit walks (Attacking → request_repath out of range), reaches melee → unit attacks (Attacking → set_target in range → CombatComponent fires per its own _sim_tick), HP bar decrements, target dies → unit transitions to Idle. Lead right-clicks a different enemy mid-attack → state transitions cleanly to a new Attacking with the new target_unit_id. Lead gives a Move command mid-attack → Attacking exits cleanly (`set_target(-1)`, cancel repath), unit walks to new target.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.16.1 (deduplicated against v0.16.0):**
  1. **Per-tick repath throttle / stale-distance threshold.** Out-of-range Attacking re-issues `request_repath` every tick. Cheap at 15 units; profile when N>50.
  2. **Click-handler enemy-right-click branch wiring (wave 2B).** This wave shipped the state in isolation; the input-side `_handle_right_click` enemy-detection branch lands in wave 2B. Until wave 2B, Attacking is reachable only via direct `transition_to` calls (e.g., from a future `UnitState_AttackMove`'s engage transition) and from headless tests.
  3. **Animation hooks (Phase 5 polish).** No animation triggering in `enter()` / `exit()` — placeholder visuals per CLAUDE.md. When real animations land, NEVER-level interrupt semantics need to play nicely with animation cancellation: a player `replace_command` mid-swing must cancel the swing animation cleanly, not just the gameplay state.
  4. **Verification-loop process bug.** This wave triggered Deviation 01 (logged in `docs/PROCESS_EXPERIMENTS.md`). The agent confused "this work appears in the tree alongside other work I didn't make" for "someone else committed my work, I'm done" — and stood down without staging. The mitigation lives in the Phase 2 session 2 kickoff brief discipline: agents are responsible for committing their own work before stand-down; TaskList is the authority on what's been completed, not `git status`.

### v0.16.2 — Phase 2 Session 1 wave 2C (2026-05-03) — ui-developer (Floating health bars + F4 attack-range overlay)

- **HealthBarsOverlay — kickoff option (b), single Control overlay over per-unit Sprite3D-Viewport.** One `_draw` call regardless of unit count. `_process` walks every Iran/Turan unit, projects through the live Camera3D, computes color-band tag + width, queue_redraws. `_draw` paints horizontal bars at the projected positions with `_BAR_HEIGHT_OFFSET = 30 px` above each unit. Color bands per kickoff §2 (8): > 70% green, 30%-70% yellow, < 30% red — boundary policy is **inclusive at the yellow band's bounds** (exactly 70% / 30% are yellow). Width by `unit_type`: kargar 32 px, piyade / turan_piyade 48 px, default fallback medium. Hidden when HP is full.

- **AttackRangeOverlay — Control + projected circle, NOT Node3D + cylinder.** `DebugOverlayManager.register_overlay(key, overlay: Control)` is statically typed against `Control`, and `toggle_overlay` does `_overlays[key] as Control` (returns null for a Node3D — F4 toggle would silently no-op). Per-frame screen projection of N circle samples produces visually identical results under any camera move. **LATER candidate**: widen `DebugOverlayManager.register_overlay(key, overlay: CanvasItem)` once a second concrete overlay needs the same affordance. Pitfall #5 candidate.

- **mouse_filter == MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE both in .tscn AND `_ready` (Pitfall #1 belt-and-braces).** Both overlays are fullscreen Controls. Third instance of the Pitfall #1 hardening pattern.

- **AttackRangeOverlay subscribes to `EventBus.selection_changed` — Pitfall #4 audit point passed.** The handler walks `SelectionManager.selected_units` (read accessor) and stashes entries on `self`. Does NOT call any SelectionManager mutator from inside the handler. Joins `selected_unit_panel.gd` and `double_click_select.gd` (defers via `call_deferred`) as the third concrete `selection_changed` consumer to ship cleanly with the cb95d09 lesson.

- **`compute_bar_entries(units, project_unit_callable)` is the public test seam.** Same shape as `box_select_handler.box_select_units`. The attack-range overlay's `handle_selection_changed(payload)` is its analogous test seam.

- **`_gather_candidate_units` is permissive (BOTH teams).** Iran AND Turan units get HP bars — combat-feel signal demands it. Phase 4 fog of war will tighten this.

- **F4 toggle path: `DebugOverlayManager.handle_function_key(KEY_F4)` → `toggle_overlay(OVERLAY_KEY_F4)` → flip `Control.visible`.** Overlay registers in `_ready`, unregisters in `_exit_tree`. F4 boots HIDDEN.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01 — refined):**

  *HealthBarsOverlay (deliverable 8):*
  1. *State that must work at runtime that no unit test exercises:* The Camera3D unproject_position projection against the live camera. `is_position_behind` filter handles units behind the camera.
  2. *What headless tests cannot detect:* Bar width readability at default zoom. Vertical offset `_BAR_HEIGHT_OFFSET = 30 px` tuned for Piyade cubes; Phase 5 cavalry/heroes may need per-unit-type offset. Color-band feel.
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test:* Lead's Piyade attacks a Turan Piyade. Bar fades green → yellow → red. Disappears when target dies.

  *AttackRangeOverlay (deliverable 9):*
  1. *State that must work at runtime that no unit test exercises:* The F4 toggle path through `DebugOverlayManager._unhandled_input`. Pitfall #4 — handler is read-only; verified by inspection.
  2. *What headless tests cannot detect:* Whether the circle's color reads as "debug viz." Whether the circle is drawn AT the unit's feet (Y=0.05 above ground). Polygon smoothness at extreme zoom.
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test:* Lead selects 5 Iran Piyade, hits F4 → 5 gold circles, radius 1.5. Lead hits F4 again → circles disappear.

- **Tests:** `tests/unit/test_health_bars_overlay.gd` (20) and `tests/unit/test_attack_range_overlay.gd` (14). +34 total. All pass headless.

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.16.2:**
  1. **Widen DebugOverlayManager.register_overlay parameter type** (Control → CanvasItem or Node). Pitfall #5 candidate.
  2. **Tween bar fade on damage** (Phase 5 polish).
  3. **Spatial-query gathering for HP bars** at high unit counts (Phase 4+, N>50).
  4. **Per-unit-type bar offset** for cavalry / heroes (Phase 5).

### v0.17.0 — Phase 2 Session 1 wave 2A (2026-05-04) — gameplay-systems (Piyade + TuranPiyade + first Farr drain)

Code shipped under commit `aa429ef` (cross-agent contamination during a parallel-wave window — ui-developer's `git commit` swept up the working-tree state which included this wave's already-completed gameplay-systems files; the wave-2A code is intact under that SHA, attribution is the only thing scrambled). This §6 entry retros the wave-2A scope.

- **Piyade is the first non-Kargar concrete Unit subclass.** Same dual `_init`+`_ready` pattern as Kargar — Godot's scene-instantiation order assigns @export defaults from the .tscn AFTER `_init`, clobbering _init's `unit_type` write; the `_ready` override fires BEFORE `super._ready()` reads unit_type to look up BalanceData. Path-string `extends "res://scripts/units/unit.gd"` to dodge the project-wide class_name registry race (see §6 v0.4.0). Stats from BalanceData: `attack_damage_x100 = 1000`, `attack_speed_per_sec = 1.0`, `attack_range = 1.5`, `max_hp 100`, `move_speed 2.5`. First read seam exercising non-zero combat fields through `Unit._apply_balance_data_defaults`.

- **TuranPiyade is the first Turan-team unit.** First `Constants.TEAM_TURAN` flow through `Unit._ready` into a `SpatialAgentComponent` for a runtime-spawned unit. Mirror-combat stats match balance-engineer wave 1C's intent.

- **`_spawn_starting_kargars` renamed to `_spawn_starting_units`.** Three position-array consts at 5 entries each = 15 starting units. Spawn order pinned: Kargar (1..5) → Iran Piyade (6..10) → Turan Piyade (11..15). Z-axis gap (Iran -8, Turan +20) means right-click engagements walk a meaningful distance.

- **First Farr drain (worker-killed-idle, -1 Farr) chosen strategy (c) — cause-string augmentation.** HealthComponent's death emit augments cause with `_idle_worker` suffix when the dying unit is a Kargar AND its FSM is in `&"idle"`. FarrSystem's `_on_unit_died` listener parses `String(cause).ends_with("_idle_worker")` and applies -1 Farr through `apply_farr_change(-1.0, "worker_killed_idle", null)` — the documented chokepoint per CLAUDE.md.

- **Why (c) over (a) and (b).** (a) extending the unit_died signature requires three cross-domain coordination points. (b) FarrSystem-side metadata Dictionary has lifetime concerns. (c) is purely additive — uses an existing signal field, no new state, forward-extensible (future drains: `_fleeing` for hero-killed-fleeing per §4, `_engaged` for hero-killed-in-battle, etc.). Cost: cause strings carry a "domain language" component documented at producer (HealthComponent) and consumer (FarrSystem._on_unit_died) sites.

- **Re-entrancy guard (cb95d09 lesson).** FarrSystem's listener confines itself to `apply_farr_change` ONLY — no SelectionManager mutation, no signal re-emit. Risk pattern that bit DoubleClickSelect → SelectionManager is structurally avoided.

- **CombatComponent passes `&"melee_attack"` as cause** (was `&"unspecified"` default). One-line change so HealthComponent's augmenter has a meaningful base cause to suffix.

- **Killer Node identity dropped at the listener boundary.** UnitRegistry autoload (now triple-LATER) would resolve `killer_unit_id: int` to a Node ref. Session 1 accepts `source_unit_id = -1` in F2 overlay log entries.

- **`reset()` re-arms the unit_died subscription idempotently.**

- **Pitfalls candidates this wave:**
  - **Pitfall #6 (candidate): Cause-string suffix conventions are domain language, not free-form telemetry.** New suffixes need explicit producer-side discipline AND consumer-side parser updates.
  - **Pitfall #7 (candidate, surfaced this session): Multi-agent shared-tree commit race.** Multiple Claude Code agents working in the same git working tree can `git add` AND `git commit` each other's working-tree changes. Mitigation: verify `git diff --staged --stat` immediately before `git commit`, AND `git log -1 --stat` after commit. Destructive resets get denied; cleanest path is to retro attribution in BUILD_LOG / ARCHITECTURE rather than rewrite history.

- **LATER items:**
  1. **`UnitRegistry` autoload.** Triple-LATER (CombatComponent target lookup, Attacking state target lookup, FarrSystem killer Node resolution).
  2. **`cause` taxonomy enum in Constants.** When ranged-attack causes land.
  3. **F2 overlay (Farr log).** Wave 2A produces F2 overlay's first non-test data point.
  4. **Friendly-fire policy.** DoD §10 open question; wave 2B's domain.
  5. **Killer Node passthrough via UnitRegistry.**

- **Coordination notes:**
  - `health_component.gd` extended ONLY in the augmenter block (wave 1A's death-emit logic unchanged).
  - `combat_component.gd` changed in exactly one line.
  - `farr_system.gd` got the `_on_unit_died` listener + `_ready` connect + `reset` re-arm.
  - `unit.gd`, `unit.tscn`, `event_bus.gd` UNTOUCHED per kickoff scope rules.
