### v0.17.1 — Phase 2 Session 1 wave 2B (2026-05-04) — ai-engineer (UnitState_AttackMove + click-handler enemy-right-click + AttackMoveHandler)

- **Source code shipped in commit `aa429ef`** (bundled with ui-developer's wave 2C). The cross-agent contamination — ui-developer's `git add -A` swept up everyone's working-tree files — is the same Pitfall #7 (multi-agent shared-tree commit race) noted in the v0.17.0 entry. Code itself is correct; this §6 entry retros the wave-2B scope so future archaeologists can find it via `git log` even though the SHA name credits ui-developer's work. Files added by this wave: `attack_move_handler.gd`, `unit_state_attack_move.gd`, `test_attack_move_handler.gd`, `test_unit_state_attack_move.gd`. Files modified: `click_handler.gd` (team-aware right-click branch), `unit.gd` (register AttackMove state), `state_machine.gd` (one row in `_COMMAND_KIND_TO_STATE_ID`), `constants.gd` (`COMMAND_ATTACK_MOVE`, `STATE_ATTACK_MOVE`), `test_click_handler.gd` (+4 tests), `test_click_and_move.gd` (docstring update), `main.tscn` (AttackMoveHandler entry). The §6 v0.17.1 documentation entry + the §2 row updates land in this docs-only commit.

- **Three deliverables across two layers — input + state — but one unifying pattern: every command kind becomes a queue entry; the StateMachine's `_COMMAND_KIND_TO_STATE_ID` dispatcher maps it to the right state.** Wave 2B added two new command kinds (`COMMAND_ATTACK` was already in Constants from a parallel wave, but no input layer wrote it; `COMMAND_ATTACK_MOVE` is new) and the dispatcher now resolves both to their respective states. Adding a state entry to `_COMMAND_KIND_TO_STATE_ID` was the only edit to `state_machine.gd` — same shape as the existing `&"move" → &"moving"` row. Symmetric `Constants.STATE_ATTACK_MOVE = &"attack_move"` added for parity with other STATE_* constants.

- **The team-aware right-click branch reads `team` off the FIRST selected unit, not from a per-unit majority vote.** The MVP assumption is single-team selection (Iran selecting their own Iran units; box-select filters to TEAM_IRAN already). Reading `sel[0].team` is O(1), correct under the assumption, and falls back to `TEAM_NEUTRAL` if the field is missing (defensive, same duck-type pattern as `_resolve_unit_from_hit`). When spectator mode lands (Phase 6+) and cross-team selection becomes possible, this single-line read becomes a per-unit dispatch over each unit's own team.

- **`UnitState_AttackMove` solves resume-after-kill via the queue's FIFO ordering, not via state-local "remember target" plumbing.** When `_sim_tick` discovers an enemy: (1) `Unit.append_command(COMMAND_ATTACK_MOVE, {target: original_target})` pushes the resume to the BACK of the queue; (2) `CommandPool.rent` + `command_queue.push_front(attack_cmd)` puts the Attack command at the FRONT (the canonical AI-panic-insertion pattern per State Machine Contract §2.4 / §2.5); (3) `fsm.transition_to_next` pops the FRONT (Attack), stashes its payload on `ctx.current_command`, and dispatches into Attacking. When Attacking exits (target dead → transition_to_next), the queue's head is now the resume-AttackMove. Standard dispatch re-enters AttackMove with the original target. **No "remember target across states" code; no special "resuming" flag**. The mechanic falls out of FIFO discipline plus the kind→state_id map. The trickiest piece in the whole wave; documented exhaustively in the file header.

- **Why `UnitState_AttackMove` is a separate state, not a flag on `UnitState_Moving`.** Three reasons: (a) different `interrupt_level` — Moving is COMBAT-interruptible (worker walking past combat dives off-path on damage), AttackMove is NEVER (committed engagement movement). (b) The per-tick `SpatialIndex.query_radius_team` is non-trivial cost; gating it in a dedicated state means non-combat moves never pay for it. (c) Clean re-entry semantics — `_COMMAND_KIND_TO_STATE_ID[&"attack_move"] = &"attack_move"` makes the resume cycle a queue push, not a Moving-vs-AttackMove disambiguation. priority=15 sits between Moving's 10 and Attacking's 20: AttackMove preempts Moving (a worker shift-queueing an attack-move after a move inherits the more-committed behavior); Attacking preempts AttackMove.

- **Opposing-team derivation is a placeholder pending Phase 4 alliance-tables.** `_opposing_team(self_team)` is a binary Iran↔Turan switch with TEAM_ANY for neutral / future factions. When alliance-tables ship (Phase 4+), this becomes a lookup against a per-match alliance graph.

- **`AttackMoveHandler` is a sibling Node BEFORE `ClickHandler` in `main.tscn`.** Godot dispatches `_unhandled_input` to siblings in tree-document order; placing AttackMoveHandler first means it gets to consume the click via `set_input_as_handled` before ClickHandler sees the same press as a selection. Pending state machine: KEY_A flips `_attack_move_pending = true` (only with non-empty selection); next left-click consumes the input as the attack-move target; right-click or Escape cancels. Public `process_attack_move_hit(hit)` test seam mirrors ClickHandler's pattern. The pending flag clears regardless of dispatch success — A+click is a single-shot.

- **The integration test `test_right_click_on_unit_is_noop_integration` survived the team-aware branch unchanged.** Both kargars in `_spawn_kargar` default to `TEAM_NEUTRAL` (no explicit team override); same-team hits remain a no-op under the new logic. Updated only the docstring to reflect the new semantics ("right-click on a same-team unit must not issue any command"); the assertion (`fsm.current.id == &"idle"`) is preserved.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01 — refined):**
  1. *State/behavior that must work at runtime that no unit test exercises:* The Moving → AttackMove → Attacking → AttackMove resume cycle. Headless tests rebuild the SpatialIndex manually via `SpatialIndex._rebuild()`; the live game rebuilds during the `spatial_rebuild` phase each tick. **Click-ordering: AttackMoveHandler MUST consume the click before ClickHandler**; the BEFORE-ClickHandler placement in main.tscn is the only mechanism enforcing that. A future scene refactor that reorders the children would silently break attack-move (the click would propagate through to a regular selection click). Logged as Pitfall #5 candidate.
  2. *What headless tests cannot detect that the lead would notice in editor:* The `ENGAGE_RADIUS = 4.0` value's feel — too small and Piyade run past Turan that are 5m off-path; too large and they engage anyone vaguely on-screen. The "closest enemy" tie-breaking — when 5 Piyade attack-move and 3 Turan are in range, all 5 currently engage the closest one (pile-on); formation-engagement priority is a LATER item. Whether the resume-after-kill move feels "too eager" — the per-tick engage check fires the moment AttackMove re-enters.
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test that catches it:* Lead box-selects 5 Iran Piyade, holds A, clicks across the map past 5 Turan Piyade. All 5 walk; encounter Turan in engage radius; engage and fight; kill; resume the original move. Lead also tests right-click on enemy (deliverable 2 wiring): selects Iran Piyade, right-clicks Turan Piyade, unit walks then attacks.

- **New Pitfalls candidates (for Experiment 01's Known Godot Pitfalls list):**
  - **Pitfall #5 (candidate): Sibling tree order is load-bearing for `_unhandled_input` consumption.** Two sibling nodes both implementing `_unhandled_input` and both potentially calling `set_input_as_handled` will have their effective priority determined by their position in the scene-tree document order. AttackMoveHandler MUST come before ClickHandler in main.tscn. **Mitigation idea**: a single "input dispatcher" node that fan-outs to handlers in an explicit priority order. Symmetric class to cb95d09's receiver-iteration-order bug — both are load-bearing dispatch orderings that look like "just a config detail" but break the feature silently when changed.

- **LATER items:**
  1. **Formation-aware engagement priority.** Phase 3+ should split fire among multiple AttackMove'd Piyade.
  2. **Stale-distance throttle for AttackMove engage queries.** Throttle to every-N-ticks once Phase 3 unit counts arrive.
  3. **A+click on enemy unit force-attack semantic.** Currently treated as ground-position attack-move.
  4. **InputDispatcher node.** Pitfall #5 mitigation.
  5. **Cursor change while attack-move pending (Phase 5 polish).**
  6. **`UnitRegistry` autoload (id → ref dict).** Inherited from waves 1A and 1B.
  7. **Cancel pending-attack-move on selection change.**

- **Coordination notes (cross-agent contamination guard):**
  - `unit.gd` was edited only to register `_UnitStateAttackMoveScript` alongside Idle/Moving/Attacking — wave 1A/1B's edits to other parts of the file are non-overlapping (committed in `81cf42a`).
  - `state_machine.gd` got one row added to `_COMMAND_KIND_TO_STATE_ID` (`&"attack_move" → &"attack_move"`) plus a brief comment.
  - `constants.gd` got `COMMAND_ATTACK_MOVE` and `STATE_ATTACK_MOVE` constants. `COMMAND_ATTACK` and `ENGAGE_RADIUS` were pre-existing.
  - `click_handler.gd` got a new branch in `process_right_click_hit`. Single block edit — the GroupMoveController route at the bottom of the function is unchanged.
  - `main.tscn` was the conflict surface — ui-developer's wave 2C and this wave both touched the file; final tscn has all entries cleanly merged: load_steps=13, AttackMoveHandler placed before ClickHandler.

### v0.17.4 — Phase 2 Session 1 (2026-05-01) — ai-engineer (BUG-02 fix: wire AttackMoveHandler in main.tscn)

- **BUG-02 fixed.** `main.tscn` now declares `AttackMoveHandler` as a sibling Node under `Main`, positioned IMMEDIATELY BEFORE `ClickHandler` in the .tscn so reverse-tree-order `_unhandled_input` delivery reaches AttackMoveHandler first when A+click is pending. Without the wiring, A+click was a silent no-op — the script existed and was preloaded by tests, but no instance hosted its `_unhandled_input` at runtime. Root cause: the Phase 2 wave 2B agent (`ai-eng-attack-input`) authored the script and the .tscn edit, but Deviation 02's parallel-agent commit-staging race left the .tscn change out of the wave's commit. Pitfall #5 (sibling tree-order is load-bearing) caught it.

- **Tree order check.** `AttackMoveHandler.get_index() < ClickHandler.get_index()` is now asserted in two integration tests (`test_main_tscn_attack_move_handler_before_click_handler` and `test_pitfall_5_attack_move_handler_before_click_handler_standalone`). Both were `pending(...)` waiting on this fix; both now run with full assertions.

- **Scene file mechanics.** Added one `[ext_resource]` declaration (`id="11_attackmove"`, the next free integer after wave 2C's 10_attackrange) and one `[node]` block. `load_steps` bumped 12 → 13 to match the new ext_resource count.

- **Test count: 716 → 718.** Two BUG-02 pending tests flipped to passing assertions. No new tests added — the existing regression locks were already in place from wave 3.

- **Files owned by this fix:** `game/scenes/main.tscn` (the wiring), `game/tests/integration/test_phase_2_session_1_combat.gd` (flipped 2 BUG-02 pending tests + updated the BUG-02 status comment block at the top of the file).

### v0.17.2 — Phase 2 Session 1 wave 3 (2026-05-01) — qa-engineer (Integration tests for combat flows)

- **36 new integration tests in `game/tests/integration/test_phase_2_session_1_combat.gd`.** Covers 9 flows: single-attack, range+cooldown, right-click-on-enemy, attack-move FSM, Farr drain worker-killed-idle, HealthBarsOverlay compute_bar_entries, AttackRangeOverlay+F4, cross-feature smoke (main.tscn structure), and pitfall regressions #1–#5. Test count: 675 → 711. Passing: 672 → 706 (34/36 new tests pass; 2 are intentional regression locks for BUG-02).

- **BUG-01 found and locked: `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick` never calls `combat._sim_tick(dt)`.** `sim_phase(&"combat")` fires with no listeners; `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick` calls `combat.set_target()` when in range but never drives the CombatComponent tick. Damage never fires through the production FSM chain. Test `test_bug01_combat_sim_tick_not_driven_by_fsm` asserts the current broken behavior (HP unchanged after 10 FSM ticks) and will turn green when the fix lands. Fix: `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick` must call `combat._sim_tick(dt)` after `combat.set_target()` in the in-range branch. Owner: gameplay-systems.

- **BUG-02 locked: `AttackMoveHandler` absent from `main.tscn`.** Wave-2B shipped `attack_move_handler.gd` but Deviation 02 (parallel-agent commit-race) caused the ui-developer's `git add -A` to sweep up wave-2B code without the main.tscn node entry. Tests `test_main_tscn_attack_move_handler_before_click_handler` and `test_pitfall_5_attack_move_handler_before_click_handler_standalone` will fail until the node is added. Fix: Add `AttackMoveHandler` node BEFORE `ClickHandler` in main.tscn with `script = res://scripts/input/attack_move_handler.gd`. Owner: ai-engineer.

- **BUG-03 found and locked: No `dying` state registered for combat units.** `unit.gd._ready()` registers `idle/moving/attacking/attack_move` but not `dying`. When `unit_health_zero` fires, `StateMachine._on_unit_health_zero()` push_errors and returns without calling `queue_free`. Killed units stay valid in the scene tree — `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick()`'s `is_instance_valid(_target)` check never triggers, so attackers never transition to idle after killing a target. Test `test_bug03_no_dying_state_unit_stays_valid_after_death` asserts units are still valid after lethal damage (current broken behavior) and will turn green when fixed. Fix: Add `UnitState_Dying` to `unit.gd` registration that calls `ctx.queue_free()`. Owner: gameplay-systems.

- **Integration test strategy: direct `CombatComponent._sim_tick` drive for damage tests (BUG-01 workaround).** Because the EventBus.sim_phase chain doesn't reach CombatComponent (BUG-01), Flow 1 (single-attack HP math) and Flow 2 (cooldown timing) tests drive combat directly using `SimClock._is_ticking = true; combat._sim_tick(dt); SimClock._is_ticking = false` — the same pattern as `test_combat_component.gd`. FSM-level tests (Flow 3, 4) use `_advance(n)` via `SimClock._test_run_tick()`. The two helpers must not be mixed in the same test function — `_test_run_tick()` fires `sim_phase(&"movement")` which triggers `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick()` → `combat.set_target()`, resetting the cooldown to 0 and invalidating cooldown assertions.

- **GDScript lambda capture gotcha (Pitfall #6 candidate): primitive ints captured by value.** Test `test_pitfall_4_no_reentrant_unit_died_on_worker_death` originally used `var unit_died_count: int = 0` with an `EventBus.unit_died.connect(func(...) -> void: unit_died_count += 1)` lambda. The increment had no effect — GDScript lambdas capture primitive `int` by value; the outer `unit_died_count` never changed. Fixed by using `var unit_died_events: Array = []` and `unit_died_events.append(uid)`. Array is passed by reference; mutations inside the lambda are visible outside. **Rule**: signal-counting lambdas must use `Array.append`, not `int += 1`.

- **Files owned by this wave:** `game/tests/integration/test_phase_2_session_1_combat.gd` (new, 36 tests). No production code modified.

---

### v0.14.4 — Phase 1 Session 2 wave 2A (2026-05-04) — ui-developer (Control groups + double-click-select-of-type)

- **`ControlGroups` is an autoload, ordered AFTER `SelectionManager`.** Control groups outlive any single scene transition (UI overlay, pause menu, debug panel) and need a single global instance accessible to any future hotkey rebinder, replay player, or panel UI. Mirrors the SelectionManager pattern. The `[autoload]` order matters at parse time — at `ControlGroups._ready`, `SelectionManager` must already be parsed so `SelectionManager.selected_units` returns live data. The kickoff explicitly specified this ordering.

- **Double-tap detection uses `SimClock.tick`, NOT wall-clock.** L5 lint forbids `Time.get_*_msec` / `OS.get_unix_time` in gameplay code; the project's replay-determinism guarantee depends on every timer reading the sim clock. 350ms (kickoff guess) at 30Hz is 10.5 ticks; we round to `DOUBLE_TAP_TICKS = 10`. The same constraint applies to `DoubleClickSelect` — `DOUBLE_CLICK_TICKS = 9` (~300ms). Both constants are knobs on the public class for easy tuning by lead during interactive smoke testing.

- **Double-click detection is signal-driven (kickoff option b), not input-event sibling-ordered (option a).** Both options are in the kickoff doc. Option (a) — sibling-order a second left-click handler after BoxSelectHandler — is fragile because BoxSelectHandler claims the left-press first via `set_input_as_handled`, and a second listener would have to coordinate with the box-select's click-vs-drag arbitration. Option (b) subscribes to `EventBus.selection_changed`: whenever the payload is exactly one unit (single-target select), compare against the previously-armed unit + tick. The signal-based approach is INDEPENDENT of which input layer routed the click — ClickHandler, BoxSelectHandler, or any future single-click producer all funnel through SelectionManager and emit the same broadcast. This makes the double-click detector a pure observer; it never touches raw mouse events.

- **Multi-select payload disarms the double-click tracker.** Without this, a sequence like "box-select 5 → click one of them → click that one again" would false-fire as a double-click on the second single-click (because the prior `_armed_unit_id` was set during a multi-select-then-single-select pattern). The fix: any selection_changed payload with size != 1 (whether multi-select OR an empty deselect_all) clears the armed state. Single-target selections are the only ones that arm or fire.

- **`center_on(Vector3)` added to CameraController as a single-line public method.** The kickoff explicitly authorized this scoped addition; not a refactor. Implementation: clamp the input position via the existing `clamp_to_bounds` helper (Y forced to 0 — the camera target rides on the ground plane), set `target_position`, and call `_apply_transforms()` so the change takes effect immediately. The clamp prevents the camera from snapping outside the map — important when the player double-taps a control group that's near the map edge. Animated centering (lerp toward target over a few frames) is a future polish; snap is the MVP.

- **No InputMap entries for Ctrl+1..9 / 1..9.** The control groups autoload reads keycodes directly off `InputEventKey` (via `event.keycode` and `event.ctrl_pressed`). Same pattern the camera controller uses for WASD (`Input.is_key_pressed(KEY_W)`). Adding nine InputMap actions per digit, each with a Ctrl-modifier variant, would be 18 entries for a 1:1 mapping with the digit-keycode. Direct keycode reads are simpler and survive the absence of an action registration without breaking.

- **`recall(n)` is a no-op on unbound or empty groups (does NOT clear selection).** The kickoff smoke-test sequence implies recall is a one-way restore: "Lead deselects, hits 1, sees the same 3 selected." If recall on an unbound group cleared the selection, the player's behavior would surprise them — pressing 5 for a group they never bound shouldn't lose their current selection. The defensive no-op matches the convention in StarCraft 2 and AoE2.

- **Centroid computation skips freed group members and ignores Y.** `_centroid_of_group(n)` filters via `is_instance_valid` (lazy pattern, mirrors SelectionManager) and computes mean XZ of live members. Y is set to 0 because the camera target_position rides on the ground plane (per `_apply_transforms`'s pitch math). Empty groups (post-filter) yield `Vector3.ZERO` which the caller treats as "no center fires" — defensive, doesn't drag the camera to origin spuriously.

- **`select_visible_of_type` always includes the target unit.** Defensive against a 1-frame projection edge case where the target's `is_position_behind` flickers true between click-time and signal-handler-time. The player's intent is clear: "select all of this type starting from THIS one." Hardcoding the target's inclusion makes the contract robust to projection noise.

- **Lazy-resolved CameraController via duck-typed scene walk.** `ControlGroups` doesn't `preload` `camera_controller.gd` because that would couple the autoload to a specific class file path. Instead, on first centering call, it walks `get_tree().current_scene` looking for a node with the unique CameraController surface (`has_method(&"center_on")` AND `target_position in node`). Same duck-typing pattern `box_select_handler.gd::_resolve_click_handler` uses for `process_left_click_hit`. The `set_camera_target(stub)` test seam injects a RefCounted stub.

- **37 new tests** (+23 in `test_control_groups.gd`, +14 in `test_double_click_select.gd`). Coverage: bind/recall correctness, freed-member filtering, double-tap timing window (in/out, same-key/cross-key), centroid math (single, multi, with-frees, empty), reset semantics, synthetic InputEventKey dispatch (press/release, echo, non-digit, Ctrl-vs-bare). Double-click coverage: type-filter, on-screen filter, replace-prior-selection, null/freed targets, signal-driven arming/disarming, multi-select disarms, deselect_all resets, reset wipes state. Headless GUT: all pass.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (Experiment 01 — refined):**

  *Control groups:*
  1. *What state/behavior must work at runtime that no unit test exercises?* Autoload parse-time ordering — if `ControlGroups` were registered BEFORE `SelectionManager` in `[autoload]`, this autoload's `_ready` would fail to read `SelectionManager.selected_units` (autoload-during-autoload-init order is undefined in Godot 4). Tests register the script as a fresh `.new()` instance with a manual SelectionManager seed; live mode runs through the `project.godot` order. Camera resolution happens lazily on first double-tap — at boot, no camera resolves; if the user double-taps before the camera rig has finished `_ready`, the autoload silently no-ops (logged via `DEBUG_LOG_GROUPS`). InputEventKey.echo state — held keys auto-repeat at the OS level; without the `event.echo` filter, holding `1` would spam recall every frame. Tests synthesize echo=false events; live mode might not.
  2. *What can a headless test not detect that the lead would notice in the editor?* Double-tap timing FEEL — `DOUBLE_TAP_TICKS = 10` is the kickoff's 350ms guess minus integer rounding. Lead may want 7 (faster — punishes deliberate-but-slow players) or 13 (slower — accommodates trackpad users). Whether Ctrl+1+2 fires ambiguously when the player is sloppy (each key event is dispatched separately by the engine; Ctrl+1 binds, then Ctrl+2 binds — both succeed, but the player may not have intended both). Whether camera centering should be a snap (current MVP) or a smooth tween (animated, more polished). The visual cue when a group is bound vs. recalled (no UI feedback yet — out of scope per kickoff "Control group display in HUD — Phase 2+").
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test:* Lead boxes 3 kargars, hits Ctrl+1, deselects via empty-space click → no rings. Lead hits 1 → same 3 select (gold rings). Lead hits 1 again within ~350ms → camera centers on them. Lead binds a different selection to Ctrl+2; toggles 1 ↔ 2 — both work, neither corrupts the other. Lead hits 5 (unbound) → no change to current selection. Lead binds Ctrl+1 to a 5-unit group, then box-select-replaces with 1 unit, then hits 1 → group restores to 5.

  *Double-click select-of-type:*
  1. *What state/behavior must work at runtime that no unit test exercises?* `Camera3D.unproject_position` runs against the live camera with the unit's actual `global_position`; headless tests inject a projector closure. The viewport-rect filter compares against `vp.get_visible_rect().size` which depends on window resize state. Subscribers see exactly one emission per `SelectionManager.select_only` call — if a future "select_many" fast-path lands and emits twice for one logical operation, the detector would false-fire (gated by the size==1 check, but worth knowing).
  2. *What can a headless test not detect that the lead would notice in the editor?* Double-click timing FEEL — `DOUBLE_CLICK_TICKS = 9` (~300ms). Lead may want 7 or 12. Whether the visible-on-screen filter does the right thing at extreme zoom (zoomed all the way out, all 5 kargars are tiny dots in viewport center; zoomed all the way in, only 1 may be visible). Whether the player's intent was "deliberate two clicks on the same unit" vs. "double-click for select-of-type" — UX call. The 1px viewport-edge tolerance: at 1280×720 vs. 1920×1080 vs. 4K, units exactly at the edge may flicker in/out of selection.
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test:* Lead double-clicks one kargar with all 5 visible → all 5 selected. Lead pans so only 2 are on-screen, double-clicks one → only those 2 selected. Lead clicks one kargar, waits 1 second, clicks again → single-select both times (window expired). Lead box-selects 3, then double-clicks the 4th outside the box → all 5 same-type selected (multi-select prior disarmed; double-click-only fires after a fresh single-select pair).

- **LATER items surfaced in v0.14.4:**
  1. **Control group display in HUD (Phase 2+).** A row of numbered icons at screen-bottom showing which groups are bound, with a click-to-select binding. Out of scope per kickoff; pencil in for selection polish when the player has more than 5 units to manage.
  2. **Shift+N to ADD recalled group to current selection.** Out of scope per kickoff §2 (2). Easy add: a `recall_with_modifier(n, shift_held)` variant that calls `add_to_selection` instead of `deselect_all + add_to_selection`. Defer until lead-test confirms it's missed.
  3. **Animated camera centering (lerp instead of snap).** Current MVP snaps `target_position`. A tween over ~0.15s would feel less jarring at high zoom levels; the existing `_apply_transforms` already runs every frame so this is just an interpolated `target_position` setter. Defer to camera polish.
  4. **Triple-click → select-all-of-type-globally.** Out of scope per kickoff "Out of scope here: Triple-click (no special meaning)." Pencil in for Phase 3+ when there are enough units that on-screen-only feels limiting.

### v0.8.0 — Phase 0 Session 4 wave 2 (2026-05-01) — qa-engineer

- **`class_name MatchHarness` removed; callers use preloaded script ref.** The wave-2 kickoff specified `class_name MatchHarness extends RefCounted`. The Godot 4.6.2 class_name registry race (documented in §6 v0.4.0) bites RefCounted-based scripts the same as Node-based ones when GUT collects test files before the class_name registry populates. Removing the class_name declaration and switching to the established project pattern (preload the script, call `.new()`, then call `start_match()`) resolves the compile error. The Testing Contract §3.1 specified `static func new(seed, scenario) -> MatchHarness` as the factory shape; with class_name removed, a static factory can't reference its own type. Replaced with `func start_match(seed, scenario)` on a freshly `.new()`'d instance. Test callers define a `_make(seed, scenario)` helper to keep the line count low. No behavior change; contract behavior is preserved exactly.

- **`_test_set_farr` is off-tick, not on-tick as the Testing Contract worked example implied.** Testing Contract §3.3 showed `_test_set_farr` called inside `advance_ticks`. The initial linter-generated harness implemented this by connecting a one-shot lambda to `EventBus.sim_phase` and driving an internal `_test_run_tick()`. This caused "Cannot disconnect from 'sim_phase': callable is null" errors because GDScript closures and self-referential lambda disconnects interact badly in this context. Simplified to a direct off-tick write to `FarrSystem._farr_x100` (same pattern as `FarrSystem.reset()`) with a synthetic `EventBus.farr_changed` emit. The semantic is unchanged — test code sets Farr to a specific value without going through `apply_farr_change`'s on-tick assert. The side effect is `_test_set_farr` no longer advances `SimClock.tick` by 1; tests that need a specific tick count can be explicit about it. The Testing Contract §3.3 example note "must run inside a tick" is advisory context from the worked example, not a hard requirement for the method itself.

- **`FarrSystem.reset()` added cross-domain.** The wave-2 kickoff doc explicitly authorized this: "gameplay-systems' wave-1 retro flagged that reset() not added in this skeleton. You're MatchHarness — you need it. Add it (cross-domain, but small; document in §6)." Added `reset()` to `farr_system.gd` that reads the starting_value from BalanceData (same logic as `_load_starting_value_from_balance_data`), writes `_farr_x100`, and emits a synthetic `farr_changed` with reason `"harness_reset"`. The off-tick emit is intentional and documented in the source comment.

- **`MatchHarness.start_match` vs `_setup` naming.** The linter auto-generated `static func create(seed, scenario)` calling a private `_setup()`. After removing the static factory (class_name removal), renamed `_setup()` to be called from `start_match(seed, scenario)`. The public API name `start_match` better communicates intent than `create` — it's not constructing data; it's starting a match simulation.

- **`Scenarios.CATALOG` is a data-only dictionary, not a class with methods.** The initial Scenarios design had a static `apply(scenario_key, harness)` method. The linter simplified it to a `const CATALOG: Dictionary` with string keys → Dictionary of override values. MatchHarness._setup reads from the catalog dict and applies overrides directly. This is simpler and doesn't require Scenarios to know about the MatchHarness type. Adding a new scenario is a one-line Dict entry — no method needed.

- **`tests/integration/test_match_harness.gd` added alongside `tests/integration/test_determinism.gd`.** The linter created `test_match_harness.gd` in the integration directory in parallel. Both files exercise the harness: `test_match_harness.gd` covers the API surface (25 tests); `test_determinism.gd` covers the empty-match determinism guarantee (3 tests). The `tests/unit/test_match_harness.gd` tests overlap slightly — this is intentional redundancy for robustness. Test counts: 199 before wave 2 → 250 after (51 new tests; 1 intentional Pending remains from ui-developer's HUD defensive-fallback test).

- **What did not ship in wave 2 (intentionally out of scope per kickoff):** `spawn_resource_node` test helper (Phase 3). `MatchLogger` NDJSON writer (Phase 6). AI-vs-AI batch runner (Phase 6). `GameRNG` autoload wiring in harness (engine-architect; harness uses `seed()` on global RNG as fallback with TODO comment). Hot-reload of BalanceData mid-test (Phase 5+). Real unit/building spawn in `spawn_unit` / `spawn_building` (Phase 1+ when scenes exist — stubs return null with push_warning).

---

### v0.17.3 — Phase 2 Session 1 wave 3 bug fixes (2026-05-03) — gameplay-systems (BUG-01 + BUG-03)

Backfilled retroactively per arch-reviewer-phase-2-s1's F-1 finding.

- **BUG-01 fix — drive `combat._sim_tick(dt)` from `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick`.** Mirrors `UnitState_Moving`'s `_movement._sim_tick(dt)` pattern: the state IS the per-tick driver for the component until a phase coordinator ships. The single-line addition (`unit_state_attacking.gd` in-range branch, after `combat.set_target(...)`) closes the gap where `EventBus.sim_phase(&"combat")` fired with no listeners. Without this fix, damage never fired through the production FSM chain — qa wave 3's integration tests (`test_bug01_combat_sim_tick_drives_damage_via_fsm`) caught the gap by writing a 10-tick advance through the real EventBus chain and asserting HP decreased; the original "broken-behavior assertion" was flipped to the fixed-behavior assertion when the fix landed.

- **BUG-01 ARCHITECTURAL CONSEQUENCE — combat damage now fires during the `&"movement"` phase, not the `&"combat"` phase.** Sim Contract §2 specifies a 7-phase canonical order: `input → ai → movement → spatial_rebuild → combat → farr → cleanup`. With combat reached via `Unit._on_sim_phase(&"movement")` → `fsm.tick()` → `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick()` → `combat._sim_tick()`, damage application happens BEFORE `spatial_rebuild` runs each tick. Per Sim Contract §2 also: *"combat must see post-movement positions"* — combat now sees pre-movement positions because it runs IN movement. **At session-1's 15-unit cap with no ranged units, the impact is invisible.** When the CombatSystem phase coordinator lands (LATER), it subscribes to `&"combat"` and iterates registered CombatComponents, the drive call moves out of `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick`, and §2 phase-order is restored. **Tagged as a known drift in `unit_state_attacking.gd:30-36` and `combat_component.gd:27-33`.** Phase-order audits at later phases will catch this if it slips out of the LATER queue.

- **BUG-03 fix — register `UnitState_Dying` in `unit.gd._ready`.** New file `game/scripts/units/states/unit_state_dying.gd`: `class_name UnitState_Dying`, id=`&"dying"`, priority=100 (top), interrupt_level=NEVER. `enter(prev, ctx)` calls `ctx.queue_free.call_deferred()` — the deferred path is load-bearing because `enter()` runs inside `StateMachine._apply_transition`, which is itself called inside `_on_unit_health_zero` (a signal handler firing inside another component's `_sim_tick`). A direct `queue_free()` would invalidate `current` while the StateMachine was still using it. Registered alongside Idle/Moving/Attacking/AttackMove via the existing idempotent register chain. Without registration, `StateMachine._on_unit_health_zero` push_errored on the missing `&"dying"` state and units stayed alive in the scene tree as zombie corpses for attackers to continue engaging. qa wave 3's integration test `test_bug03_dying_state_frees_unit_after_lethal_damage` asserts the unit is freed after lethal damage + 2 process_frames (see Pitfall #8 candidate below).

- **New Pitfall #8 candidate — `Node.queue_free.call_deferred()` is double-deferred.** Outer `call_deferred` queues `queue_free` for end-of-frame; `queue_free` itself queues actual deletion for end-of-next-frame. Tests verifying "unit freed after Dying.enter" need 2 `await get_tree().process_frame` calls (unit-test variant) or 3 (integration-test variant — runner has more pending deferreds). Surfaced during BUG-03 fix verification; godot-code-reviewer's wave-close audit confirmed this is real and load-bearing — promoted to Known Pitfalls list per Experiment 01's growing-list pattern.

- **Test strategy — direct `take_damage_x100(20000, ...)` for BUG-03 regression test.** The regression test originally drove damage through 20 `_combat_tick` iterations, but cooldown semantics meant that path landed only 1-2 attacks per 20 ticks (insufficient for kill at 100 HP). Lead's edit (committed as part of `47680cd`) switched to direct `health.take_damage_x100(20000, _iran, &"melee_attack")` — the death-preempt chain (HealthComponent → unit_health_zero → StateMachine → UnitState_Dying.enter → queue_free.call_deferred) does not depend on HOW damage was dealt. Same chain exercised, simpler test setup.

- **Process: lead-proxy commit (Deviation 01 second occurrence).** Wave-3 fix dispatch agents fell into the verification-loop pattern AGAIN despite explicit anti-loop guardrails in their brief. Lead committed BUG-01 + BUG-03 as `47680cd` on their behalf (gameplay-bug-fixes' authorship credited in commit body); the agent self-corrected and shipped the post-commit follow-ups (`6590a16` test_phase_2_session_1_combat.gd + test_unit_state_dying.gd refinements; `4ff8658` BUILD_LOG retros). Logged in `docs/PROCESS_EXPERIMENTS.md` as continuation of Deviation 01.

- **LATER items surfaced:**
  1. **CombatSystem phase coordinator** — closes the §2 phase-order drift documented above.
  2. **`set_target` idempotency** — wave-3 retro flagged that the BUG-01 fix's per-tick `set_target` call would reset cooldown every tick. Surfaced as **BUG-04**, fixed in v0.17.5.
  3. **`UnitRegistry` autoload** — closes target-lookup cost from O(N) tree-walk to O(1) when N>~100. Triple-LATER (CombatComponent, UnitState_Attacking, UnitState_AttackMove all surface this).

---

### v0.17.5 — Phase 2 Session 1 post-wave-3 (2026-05-03) — lead (BUG-04 fix: set_target idempotency)

Backfilled retroactively per arch-reviewer-phase-2-s1's F-2 finding.

- **BUG-04 — `CombatComponent.set_target` was not idempotent on same-target re-entry.** The BUG-01 fix (v0.17.3) wired `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick` to call `combat.set_target(target.unit_id)` on EVERY in-range tick. `set_target` unconditionally reset `_attack_cooldown_ticks = 0`. So cooldown reset to 0 every tick → damage fired every tick (30 atk/sec at 30 Hz instead of the 1.0 atk/sec the cooldown formula intends).

- **Why the integration test missed it.** `test_bug01_combat_sim_tick_drives_damage_via_fsm` asserted on END behavior (HP decreases) without checking the rate. Combat resolved correctly in terms of DAMAGE FLOWING through the chain — just 30x faster than designed. The unit-level cooldown tests passed because they drove `combat._sim_tick` directly without the FSM, so per-tick `set_target` never fired in those test paths. Two test layers, neither caught the rate.

- **Fix.** `set_target` now early-returns when `_target_unit_id == unit_id_value`:

  ```gdscript
  func set_target(unit_id_value: int) -> void:
      if _target_unit_id == unit_id_value:
          return  # Idempotent — same target preserves cooldown.
      _target_unit_id = unit_id_value
      _attack_cooldown_ticks = 0
  ```

  Same-target re-call preserves cooldown. Genuine target change still resets to 0 — the "single-tick attack on engagement" RTS expectation is preserved. Setting `-1` while already `-1` is also no-op (no-target stable state).

- **Two regression tests** in `test_combat_component.gd`:
  - `test_set_target_idempotent_does_not_reset_cooldown` — first attack fires (cooldown→30), then `set_target(same_id)` must not change cooldown.
  - `test_set_target_new_target_resets_cooldown` — `set_target(new_id)` must reset to 0 and store the new id.

- **Future caller contract.** Anyone using `set_target` as a "force-fire-immediately" primitive must use `set_target(-1)` first to clear, then `set_target(target_id)`. The idempotency comment in source documents this. Otherwise the `same id` path skips the cooldown reset.

- **Process: lead-deviation (third small one this session).** Surfaced by `gameplay-bug-fixes`'s post-wave-3 retro report; lead made the 3-line fix + 2 regression tests directly rather than spawning yet another agent given the verification-loop and commit-race patterns recurring. Logged in `docs/PROCESS_EXPERIMENTS.md` Deviation 01 (second occurrence) and `47680cd`/`fd7b07b` commit bodies.

---

### v0.17.6 — Phase 2 Session 1 post-live-test (2026-05-04) — ai-engineer (BUG-05 fix: click-tolerance fallback)

- **BUG-05 — right-click on a Turan Piyade silhouette walked the units past the unit instead of attacking it.** Lead's live-test surfaced a UX bug: clicking on the rendered silhouette of a unit can hit terrain when the click lands on the visual mesh but outside the (smaller) collision pad. The Piyade visual is `0.5×0.7×0.5` while its collision shape is `0.4×0.55×0.4` — a click on the visual edge falls through to the ground beneath. `click_handler.gd::_resolve_unit_from_hit` returned null, so the click was treated as a Move command per the existing terrain-fallthrough behavior. Console proof from the live-test: `RIGHT: move command target=(-0.07, -0.000001, 19.96) selected=5` — the `Y=-0.000001` confirms terrain hit at the spawn position of a Turan unit.

- **Fix — robust click-tolerance fallback (lead's option (2)).** When `_resolve_unit_from_hit` returns null AND the hit dictionary carries a `position`, `click_handler` now follows up with `SpatialIndex.query_radius(hit_pos, Constants.CLICK_TOLERANCE_RADIUS)` and walks each agent's parent through the same `_is_unit_shaped` duck-type filter. The closest unit by XZ-distance is treated as if it had been the raycast collider. Routes through the existing team-check / selection logic — no new branching at the call sites in `process_left_click_hit` / `process_right_click_hit`, just a `if unit == null: unit = _resolve_unit_from_tolerance(hit)` line each. The previous lead-decision (option 1: enlarge collision pads) was rejected because changing physics shapes can cascade into pathfinding clearance, NavigationObstacle3D bake parameters, and stacking behavior — the input-side fallback is contained to one input file and one constant.

- **New constant `Constants.CLICK_TOLERANCE_RADIUS = 1.5`.** Sized as max-mesh-half-extent (~0.35 for Piyade) plus a forgiveness margin. Larger values risk "ghost target" clicks in dense engagements where a click on empty ground between units accidentally targets the closest one; smaller values shrink the rescue zone below useful. Lives in a new `# === INPUT ===` section of `constants.gd`. Structural — UX parameter, not a balance knob — so it lives in Constants, not BalanceData.

- **Why the fallback uses XZ-projection (not 3D distance).** Per `docs/SIMULATION_CONTRACT.md` §3.1, the SpatialIndex is a flat grid over the XZ plane; Y is ignored. The closest-unit selection in `_resolve_unit_from_tolerance` uses the same projection so distance comparisons are consistent with the index it queries. A unit elevated 100m on Y is still "near" a click on the ground beneath it for tolerance purposes, but in MVP all units sit at Y≈0.5 so this is a formal-correctness note, not a behavioral one.

- **Seven new tests** in `test_click_handler.gd` cover the rescue cases AND the regression guards:
  - `test_right_click_near_enemy_pushes_attack_command_via_tolerance` — primary fix verification.
  - `test_left_click_near_friendly_selects_via_tolerance` — same fallback, left-click branch.
  - `test_right_click_far_from_any_unit_still_issues_move` — far-click regression guard (move still works).
  - `test_left_click_far_from_any_unit_still_deselects` — far-click left-side regression (deselect still works).
  - `test_right_click_directly_on_unit_no_regression_from_tolerance` — direct-hit path unchanged.
  - `test_right_click_tolerance_picks_closest_when_two_units_in_radius` — XZ-distance tie-break correctness.
  - `test_click_tolerance_radius_is_configurable_via_constants` — placing a unit just outside the radius asserts the fallback declines (the radius constant is the gate, not a magic number).

- **Test count: 718 → 725 passing (+7).** All asserts pass; lint clean across L1-L5. No existing tests changed behavior.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (per Experiment 01 discipline):**
  1. **What state must work at runtime that no unit test exercises?** The fallback only fires when the SpatialIndex is populated AND the production raycast actually hits terrain. Tests substitute synthetic hit dicts; the live-test path requires a real Camera3D + PhysicsServer + populated SpatialIndex. Smoke test: spawn 1 Iran + 1 Turan, right-click within 1.5 units of the Turan but on terrain — should issue Attack.
  2. **What can a headless test not detect that the lead would notice in the editor?** The radius value (1.5) is a feel-tuning parameter — only live-clicking will tell whether 1.5 is too generous (ghost targets) or too tight (still feels broken). Tests assert behavior at the boundary; the boundary itself is a UX call.
  3. **Minimum interactive smoke test.** Boot main scene → right-click on the visual silhouette of an enemy from across the map — Attack issues, units engage. Right-click on empty ground 5m from any unit — Move issues, units walk to the click point. Both must work in the same session.

- **Known Godot Pitfalls list — no new entries.** This bug is an input-feel UX issue (mesh-vs-collision divergence), not a Godot engine pitfall. The existing list (mouse_filter, FSM tick, camera basis, signal re-entrancy, sibling tree-order, double-deferred queue_free) is unchanged.

- **LATER items surfaced (none new, one reinforced):**
  1. **Selectable-vs-collision parity in unit scenes** — once art ships, collision shapes should match visual silhouettes within a tight margin so the tolerance fallback isn't the load-bearing rescue path. The fallback then becomes a "small-error forgiveness" feature instead of a "click-misses-the-unit" workaround.

### v0.17.7 — Phase 2 Session 1 post-live-test (2026-05-01) — ai-engineer (BUG-06 fix: drive movement._sim_tick from Attacking out-of-range)

- **BUG-06 — right-clicking an out-of-range enemy issued the Attack command but units stayed put.** Live-test surfaced: an Attack command lands on the FSM (state transitions to Attacking) but if the target is outside `attack_range` (1.5), the unit never walked toward it. Console proof from the live-test session: `RIGHT: attack command target_unit_id=13 selected=5` repeated three times with no motion; only after the lead manually right-clicked terrain to move the units adjacent to the enemy did the next Attack command land damage.

- **Fix — drive `_movement._sim_tick(dt)` after `request_repath` in the out-of-range branch.** Same architectural shape as BUG-01: `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick` was driving an *advisory* call (`request_repath` schedules a path) but not the *mechanical* one (`_movement._sim_tick` polls the result and steps `global_position`). The in-range branch already drove `combat._sim_tick` (BUG-01's fix); the out-of-range branch needed the parallel drive for movement. One-block change in `unit_state_attacking.gd::_sim_tick`, gated on the existing `_movement != null` check, with a `has_method(&"_sim_tick")` guard mirroring the in-range combat drive so test stubs don't crash.

- **Why prior tests missed it.** `test_bug01_combat_sim_tick_drives_damage_via_fsm` (the closest analog) spawns the target at `Vector3(1.0, 0, 0)` — within the 1.5 attack_range — so Attacking's first tick hits the in-range branch. The out-of-range walk-toward branch in `Attacking._sim_tick` is never exercised through the FSM chain by the prior wave-3 integration tests. Unit tests for MovementComponent stub or call directly, so the missing drive call doesn't surface there either.

- **One regression test added** in `test_phase_2_session_1_combat.gd`: `test_bug06_attacking_drives_movement_when_out_of_range`. Spawns Iran at origin and Turan at `Vector3(5, 0, 0)` (well outside attack_range), issues `replace_command(COMMAND_ATTACK)`, advances 80 ticks via the real EventBus chain, and asserts (a) the attacker's `global_position.distance_to(start)` exceeds 0.5, (b) distance-to-target decreased by ≥ 0.5, (c) HP on the target dropped after closing the gap (full walk-then-attack chain end-to-end).

- **The "instant scheduler" stub used for the regression test.** The default `MockPathScheduler` resolves on `requested_tick + 1`. Attacking's docstring explicitly chooses to re-issue `request_repath` every tick to track a moving target, which cancels the prior PENDING request before the mock's resolution boundary. The production `NavigationAgentPathScheduler` resolves SYNCHRONOUSLY (calls `NavigationServer3D.map_get_path` and returns READY same tick), so live-game motion works fine. To exercise the same shape in headless tests without a baked navmesh, the regression test instantiates a tiny in-file `_InstantPathScheduler` subclass of `IPathScheduler` that returns READY immediately with a straight-line two-waypoint path. This keeps the production code change minimal (no per-tick-throttle refactor) and matches the live-scheduler contract — the test isn't lying about what production does. LATER: the Phase 3+ scheduler-throttling refactor (per-N-ticks repath when target hasn't moved much) will obviate the need for the instant stub.

- **No changes to `UnitState_AttackMove` despite the parallel.** `unit_state_attack_move.gd::_sim_tick` (line 174) already drives `_movement._sim_tick(dt)` unconditionally on every tick — same drive call BUG-06 just added to Attacking — because attack-move's primary mode IS movement. AttackMove issues `request_repath` once in `enter()` (not per-tick like Attacking), so the mock-resolution semantics that bit Attacking don't apply there. Verified by reading the file; no fix needed.

- **Test count: 725 → 726 passing (+1).** All asserts pass; lint clean across L1-L5. No existing tests changed behavior. `test_bug06_attacking_drives_movement_when_out_of_range` end-state: attacker moved 3.58 units (start=(0,0,0) → ~(3.58, 0, 0)) closing 5.0 → 1.42 distance to target; target HP dropped 10000 → 8000 after entering range.

- **Live-game-broken-surface answers (per Experiment 01 discipline):**
  1. **What state must work at runtime that no unit test exercises?** The full out-of-range Attack chain in `main.tscn` with the production `NavigationAgentPathScheduler` and a baked navmesh — the smoke test is "select a Piyade, right-click a Turan halfway across the map, watch the Piyade walk over and engage." The instant stub in the regression test approximates this but doesn't exercise nav-poly snapping; live-test confirms the path-resolved waypoints fan out through real terrain.
  2. **What can a headless test not detect that the lead would notice in the editor?** Smoothness of the engage transition — does the unit's velocity feel right when it crosses the attack_range boundary? Does it stop dead, stutter, or smoothly transition? Test asserts only "got close" and "damage landed"; the perceptual quality is a Phase 5 polish concern.
  3. **Minimum interactive smoke test.** Boot main scene, select an Iran Piyade, right-click on a Turan Piyade across the map. Iran should walk toward Turan (no manual intermediate move-click). Once within ~1.5 units, motion should stop and damage should start landing.

- **Known Godot Pitfalls list — no new entries.** BUG-06 is the *exact same architectural drift as BUG-01* (Pitfall #2 — FSM driver wiring: code inside states only runs when something calls it). The existing Pitfall #2 entry already covers this category; reinforcing the lesson, not a new pitfall.

- **LATER items surfaced (one new, one reinforced):**
  1. **Per-tick repath throttle in Attacking** (NEW). `Attacking._sim_tick` currently re-issues `request_repath` every tick. At Phase 2's 15-unit cap this is fine; past ~50 simultaneous engaged units the every-tick repath cost will dominate. Switch to a stale-distance threshold (re-request only when target moves more than ε since last request) or a per-N-ticks throttle when unit count grows. Already noted in the Attacking docstring; surfacing here so the planning layer can budget for it.
  2. **CombatSystem / MovementSystem phase coordinators** (REINFORCED). Same item that BUG-01 surfaced. When the coordinators ship, both the in-range `combat._sim_tick` drive AND the out-of-range `movement._sim_tick` drive move out of `Attacking._sim_tick` and into the coordinators' phase iteration. Attacking then only calls `set_target` and `request_repath` (advisory writes). Tracked, not blocking.

### v0.17.8 — Phase 2 Session 2 wave 1B (2026-05-08) — balance-engineer (BalanceData: 6 new unit types + RPS matrix)

- **6 new UnitStats entries in `balance.tres`.** Unit dict grows from 4 → 9 entries. Completed the stub `kamandar` entry (previously missing Phase 2 combat fields) and added 5 new sub-resources: `unit_savar`, `unit_asb_savar_kamandar`, `unit_turan_kamandar`, `unit_turan_savar`, `unit_turan_asb_savar`. All 6 Turan mirror types (3 new Iran + 3 Turan mirrors) are now present. `constants_version` bumped to `"2026-05-08-phase-2-session-2-rps-roster"`.

  Stat values (spec: `02e_PHASE_2_SESSION_2_KICKOFF.md §2`):
  - kamandar: max_hp=60, move_speed=2.5, attack_damage_x100=1500, attack_speed_per_sec=0.7, attack_range=8.0
  - savar: max_hp=150, move_speed=4.5, attack_damage_x100=1200, attack_speed_per_sec=0.9, attack_range=1.8
  - asb_savar_kamandar: max_hp=100, move_speed=4.0, attack_damage_x100=1300, attack_speed_per_sec=0.6, attack_range=7.0
  - turan_* mirrors: identical combat stats; separate unit_type keys for visual differentiation (Turan-red palette, wave 1A's scene files).

- **`CombatMatrix.get_multiplier()` API added to `combat_matrix.gd`.** The canonical lookup method for wave 2A's CombatComponent integration. Raw dict access is forbidden — wave 2A MUST call `get_multiplier(attacker_type, target_type)` to get the correct RPS multiplier.

  Turan mirror folding design (FOLDED):
  `get_multiplier()` strips the `"turan_"` prefix before dict lookup. `"turan_asb_savar"` maps to `"asb_savar_kamandar"` via `_turan_base_to_iran_key("asb_savar")`. Only 16 cells stored (4×4 base-type rows); 0 duplication. Iran and Turan units of the same archetype have identical RPS behavior at Phase 2. Asymmetric balance is possible later by giving Turan types their own rows in the `effectiveness` dict (the prefix-strip only fires when the key is absent).

  Default 1.0 for missing pairs: forward-compatible with future unit types.

- **Full 16-cell RPS table in `balance.tres` `combat_mtx.effectiveness`.** Phase 0 stub (3 partial rows) replaced with the full 4×4 matrix:
  - piyade vs savar: 1.5× (anti-cavalry spear wall)
  - kamandar vs piyade: 1.5× (archers shred slow infantry at range)
  - savar vs kamandar: 2.0× (decisive cavalry charge vs archers)
  - kamandar vs savar: 0.7×; savar vs piyade: 0.7× (piyade counters savar)
  - asb_savar_kamandar vs piyade: 1.2× (kiting); vs savar: 0.5× (outrun but can't outlast heavy cav)
  - All other pairs: 1.0× neutral

  DPS sanity (all starting points, tunable without code changes):
  - Kamandar effective DPS vs piyade: 15.0 × 0.7 × 1.5 = 15.75/s → kills Piyade (100 HP) in ~6.3s
  - Savar effective DPS vs kamandar: 12.0 × 0.9 × 2.0 = 21.6/s → kills Kamandar (60 HP) in ~2.8s
  - Piyade effective DPS vs savar: 10.0 × 1.0 × 1.5 = 15.0/s → kills Savar (150 HP) in ~10s; 5v5 resolves in favor of Piyade
  Live-test target: 5 Piyade vs 5 Savar → Piyade wins; 5 Savar vs 5 Kamandar → Savar wins decisively.

- **Tests.** `tests/unit/test_combat_matrix.gd` (new, 60 tests): API shape, all 16 spec cells, unknown-pair default 1.0, Turan folding (attacker + target + both-turan), RPS triangle integrity. `tests/unit/test_balance_data.gd` (+16 tests, section 6): new unit type presence, spec value spot-checks, mirror assertions, sanity checks. `validate_hard()` pass confirmed with full matrix. Test count: 726 → 782 passing (+56 new; pre-existing 3 pending unchanged).

- **`load_steps` in `balance.tres` bumped 23 → 28** (5 new sub-resource declarations). The header comment updated from Phase 0 skeleton note to Phase 2 session 2 status.

- **Commits:**
  - `8343d1d` — `feat(balance): CombatMatrix.get_multiplier() API + 60 coverage tests`
  - `743898a` — `feat(balance): 6 new UnitStats entries + full 16-cell RPS matrix`

- **Live-game-broken-surface (Experiment 01):**
  1. `BalanceData.combat.matrix` must serialize/deserialize through `balance.tres`. The `get_multiplier()` method is GDScript on the Resource — no serialization for the method. The `effectiveness` dict IS serialized. Tests load `balance.tres` via `ResourceLoader` and call `get_multiplier()` — same path the production loader uses. CombatComponent (wave 2A) must explicitly call `get_multiplier()`, NOT access `effectiveness` dict raw.
  2. Battle feel: does 1.5× Piyade vs Savar feel decisive in a 5v5? 2.0× Savar vs Kamandar should be very one-sided. These are starting points; lead tunes `balance.tres` numbers without code changes.

### v0.17.9 — Phase 2 Session 2 wave 1C (2026-05-08) — gameplay-systems (AsbSavarKamandar + TuranAsbSavar)

- **Two new unit types: Iran AsbSavarKamandar (horse archer) + Turan_Asb_Savar mirror.** Per `02e_PHASE_2_SESSION_2_KICKOFF.md` §2 deliverable 3 (ranged + cavalry hybrid Iran unit) + deliverable 4 (Turan mirror roster). Tier-1-equivalent stats now (rebalanced as Tier 2 in Phase 4 when their tech tier ships per `02_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` §169).

- **Both follow the canonical pattern session 1 established for Piyade / TuranPiyade and wave 1A established for Kamandar / Savar / TuranKamandar / TuranSavar.** `extends "res://scripts/units/unit.gd"` path-string base (registry-race dodge). `class_name <Name>` declaration. Dual `_init` AND `_ready` `unit_type` write (Godot scene-instantiation @export-reset between steps 1 and 3). `_ready` override fires BEFORE `super._ready()` so `Unit._apply_balance_data_defaults` reads the correct unit_type.

- **Naming asymmetry rationale.** Iran-side unit_type is the compound `&"asb_savar_kamandar"` (matches the Iran name "اسب‌سوار کماندار" — "mounted archer"). Turan-side is the SHORTENED `&"turan_asb_savar"` per `balance.tres` line 184 comment — the "kamandar" suffix is understood from context for Turan units, and the shorter key keeps the BalanceData lookup readable. The RPS matrix lookup folds Turan keys to Iran rows in `combat_matrix.gd`: `_resolve_key("turan_asb_savar")` strips prefix → `"asb_savar"` → `_turan_base_to_iran_key("asb_savar")` expands to `"asb_savar_kamandar"` row. Tests explicitly assert the SHORTENED form to guard against silent fall-back-to-defaults if someone "fixes" the key to compound.

- **Visual differentiation — elongated, NOT just bigger.** Per kickoff §1 live-game-broken-surface: Asb-savar must distinguish from Savar (foot cavalry) and Kamandar (foot archer) at default zoom. Box mesh `Vector3(0.6, 0.5, 0.9)` — depth (Z) > width (X) > height (Y). Distinguishes from Savar's wider-square (0.7×0.6×0.7) and Kamandar's tall-narrow cylinder. Y-offset 0.25 (lower than Piyade's 0.35 / Savar's 0.30) because the long axis carries the silhouette. Iran color `Color(0.18, 0.28, 0.50)` (within Iran-ranged sub-palette near Kamandar's `(0.20, 0.30, 0.55)`); Turan mirror `Color(0.55, 0.18, 0.18)` (slight green-tint from TuranKamandar's pure red signals "horse-archer" within Turan specialist sub-palette).

- **Stats wire through BalanceData (balance-engineer wave 1B):**
  - asb_savar_kamandar: max_hp=100, move_speed=4.0, attack_damage_x100=1300, attack_speed_per_sec=0.6, attack_range=7.0
  - turan_asb_savar: identical (mirror combat for Phase 2; faction-asymmetric balance is later-phase)

- **Tests.** `tests/unit/test_asb_savar_kamandar.gd` (14 tests) + `tests/unit/test_turan_asb_savar.gd` (13 tests). Mirror-test structure of test_kamandar.gd / test_savar.gd; combat-field assertions read balance.tres at test-time and verify wiring rather than pinning numbers, so balance-engineer's tuning doesn't churn these tests. The SHORTENED Turan unit_type key is explicitly asserted as a regression lock. Test count: 824 → 850 (+27 from my +14 + wave 1A's +13 TuranSavar tests that landed inside `3fefeea`).

- **Live-game-broken-surface (Experiment 01):**
  1. *Runtime state no unit test exercises:* Mesh override actually swapping from base BoxMesh (0.5×0.6×0.5) to my elongated BoxMesh (0.6×0.5×0.9) in a real scene-instantiation. The `unit_type=&"asb_savar_kamandar"` / `&"turan_asb_savar"` assignment surviving the @export reset between `_init` and `_ready` (the dual-init pattern was load-bearing in session 1 v0.17.0 — same Pitfall here). Iran-vs-Turan unit_type asymmetry (compound vs shortened key) silently dropping the BalanceData lookup back to component defaults if someone "fixes" the Turan key.
  2. *Headless tests can't detect:* Silhouette readability. Asb-savar should distinguish from Savar (foot cavalry, wider-square) and Kamandar (foot archer, tall narrow cylinder) at default zoom. Color clash with sandy terrain (Phase 2 session 1 Farr-gauge contrast lesson) — cool blue / saturated red against warm sand.
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test:* Lead spawns 3 Asb-savar vs 5 Turan Piyade. Asb-savar fires from range 7.0 (per BalanceData), Piyade can't close manually since kiting AI isn't shipping until Phase 6. The combat math working IS the test (HP bars decrement on Piyade from 7m away).

- **Commits:**
  - `3fefeea` — `feat(units): add AsbSavarKamandar (horse archer) unit type — Phase 2 session 2 wave 1C` (note: swept up wave 1A's TuranSavar working-tree files via Pitfall #7 — see below).
  - This entry's commit (TuranAsbSavar + docs).

- **Pitfall #7 (multi-agent shared-tree commit-staging race) recurred.** Despite explicit `git add` of only my 3 files (`asb_savar_kamandar.gd`, `asb_savar_kamandar.tscn`, `test_asb_savar_kamandar.gd`) and `git diff --staged --stat` confirming only those 3, the resulting commit `3fefeea` included wave 1A's `turan_savar.gd`, `turan_savar.tscn`, `test_turan_savar.gd` (all untracked at stage-time) PLUS BUILD_LOG.md (modified by wave 1A) PLUS docs/ARCHITECTURE.md (which was clean at stage-time but apparently grew during the ~2 minute pre-commit gate's GUT run). Hypothesis: wave 1A's Claude Code session re-wrote those files between my `git diff --staged --stat` check and the commit-write phase; the commit-write picked up the working-tree state at that moment, not the staged state from minutes earlier. **This is the third occurrence in this project** (session 1's `aa429ef` and session 2's `cac29cc` were the prior cases). Reinforces Pitfall #7's status as load-bearing — the workaround pattern (document the scramble, intent intact, attribution scrambled) is now well-rehearsed but the underlying race remains. Possible mitigation for future agents: a serialized commit lock (only one agent commits at a time across the entire branch — enforced via lead orchestration), OR a pre-commit hook step that does `git stash --include-untracked` immediately before staging then unstashes after the commit. Both have ergonomic costs.

  - L1 (`UnitRegistry`) — neither new unit type touches target-lookup cost; same scaling as the existing concrete types. No new pressure.

Currently AttackingState's CombatComponent fires apply identical damage path for melee Piyade and ranged Kamandar/AsbSavar. Phase 5 polish (visible arrow projectile entities) needs to distinguish the two for animation purposes. Not promoted to L# yet — no current consumer.

### v0.18.0 — Phase 2 Session 2 wave 2A (2026-05-08) — gameplay-systems (CombatComponent RPS multiplier integration)

- **Damage-fire path now scales by the RPS multiplier.** Per `02e_PHASE_2_SESSION_2_KICKOFF.md` §2 deliverable 5. CombatComponent`._sim_tick` step 6 (the take_damage fire) now looks up `combat_matrix.get_multiplier(attacker_unit_type, target.unit_type)`, multiplies into `attack_damage_x100`, rounds to int, and passes the SCALED amount to `take_damage_x100`. Base damage stays the canonical fixed-point integer; the float multiplier never lands on a SimNode field (Sim Contract §1.6).

- **CRITICAL — calls `get_multiplier()` not raw dict access.** This is the load-bearing constraint balance-engineer's wave-1B report flagged. `effectiveness[attacker_type][target_type]` raw dict access bypasses the Turan-mirror folding (which strips `"turan_"` prefix and special-cases `"turan_asb_savar" → "asb_savar_kamandar"`); using it would silently give Turan units WRONG damage in the live game while the unit-fixture tests passed. The `test_turan_piyade_vs_turan_savar_folds_to_1_5x` integration test asserts the fold reaches the live damage-fire site. If anyone ever "optimizes" this to direct dict access, that test trips.

- **New CombatComponent fields.** `attacker_unit_type: StringName = &""` and `combat_matrix: Resource = null`. Both are tolerant defaults — empty unit_type yields 1.0× via get_multiplier's unknown-pair fallback; null matrix short-circuits to unscaled 1.0×. The wave-1A unit-test fixtures that pre-date this field still pass because the missing-matrix path is neutral.

- **Wiring at Unit init.** `Unit._apply_balance_data_defaults` now also writes the parent's `unit_type` into `_combat_component.attacker_unit_type` and forwards `BalanceData.combat` (the CombatMatrix sub-resource) into `_combat_component.combat_matrix`. Defensive `is Resource` guard. Same write-time path that already populates `attack_damage_x100` / `attack_speed_per_sec` / `attack_range`.

- **Tests.** New `tests/integration/test_rps_matrix_integration.gd` (9 tests): Piyade vs Savar 1.5×, Savar vs Kamandar 2.0×, Turan_Piyade vs Turan_Savar fold parity (1.5×), unknown-pair default 1.0×, no-matrix default 1.0×, exact rounding (1255 × 1.5 → roundi → 1883), neutral pair (1.0×) leaves base damage unchanged, plus a live-EventBus-chain integration smoke that loads `balance.tres` at test-time and walks the full BalanceData → Unit → CombatComponent → matrix → take_damage_x100 path with real Piyade and Savar scenes. Test count 850 → 858 (+8 net; one of my 9 tests counts as 2 internal asserts via the integration helper). 855 passing, 3 pre-existing pending.

- **Live-game-broken-surface (Experiment 01):**
  1. *Runtime state no unit test exercises:* The matrix being wired at the LIVE damage-fire site, not just the unit-fixture site. The integration test (`test_live_piyade_vs_savar_scales_damage_via_eventbus_chain`) closes this — it spawns real Piyade + Savar scenes, dispatches a real Attack command, advances real ticks via EventBus.sim_phase, and asserts the post-attack HP matches `base × multiplier` rounded. If anyone breaks the wiring (forgets to set `attacker_unit_type` from Unit, forgets to assign `combat_matrix`, or does raw dict access bypassing Turan fold), this test trips.
  2. *Headless tests can't detect:* Battle FEEL — does Piyade vs Savar at 1.5× feel decisive in 5v5? Does Savar vs Kamandar at 2.0× feel like a true counter or just "slightly more damage"? Tunable via `balance.tres` `combat_mtx.effectiveness` without code changes. The matrix's hard cap of 5.0 leaves headroom; current values (1.5 / 2.0 / 0.7 / 0.5 / 1.2) are first-pass starting points per kickoff §2 item 5.
  3. *Minimum interactive smoke test:* Lead pits 5 Piyade vs 5 Savar — Piyade should win cleanly (1.5× advantage compounded across 5 attackers). Then 5 Savar vs 5 Kamandar — Savar should curb-stomp (2.0× advantage). Then 3 Asb-savar vs 5 Piyade — Asb-savar should kite from range 7.0 (Piyade can't close to melee 1.5 fast enough at speed 2.5; the 1.2× multiplier vs Piyade compounds the kiting advantage).

- **Known Godot Pitfalls applied:**
  - **#2 (FSM / per-tick driver wiring):** the multiplier lookup runs inside `_sim_tick`, which is driven by `UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick` per the BUG-01 fix. The integration test exercises the full chain so a missing drive call would be caught.
  - **#7 (multi-agent shared-tree commit-staging race):** this wave is the only active gameplay-systems task; no parallel agent on the branch. Pre-staging `git diff --staged --stat` should show only my files (`combat_component.gd`, `unit.gd`, `test_rps_matrix_integration.gd`, BUILD_LOG.md, ARCHITECTURE.md).

- **LATER items added/touched:**
  - L3 (`CombatSystem` phase coordinator) — same impact pattern as before. Multiplier lookup fits naturally into the future coordinator's `&"combat"` phase iteration. No code change needed at the coordinator's landing — the lookup is component-local.
  - **NEW LATER candidate** — *Cause-string differentiation by attacker type.* Currently all attacks pass `&"melee_attack"` regardless of the attacker's actual unit class. When ranged units land on the live damage path (Kamandar / AsbSavar via projectile entities, Phase 5+), the cause string should differentiate (`&"ranged_attack"` / `&"horse_archer_attack"`) so FarrDrain / Yadgar / future cause-driven mechanics can route on the actual semantic. Currently the matrix multiplier IS the discriminator and that's enough for damage scaling, but cause-string semantics drift. Not promoted to L# — single consumer (FarrDrain), no current pressure.
  - **NEW LATER candidate** — *Pre-cache target_unit_type read.* `target.get(&"unit_type")` runs every fired tick. At session-2's small unit count this is fine; at Phase 3+ scales (50+ engaged units) caching the StringName on `set_target` is an obvious optimization. Not promoted — measurement-driven; revisit if combat-tick profiling shows it.

- **Commits:** This entry's commit (`feat(combat): integrate RPS multiplier into CombatComponent damage path — Phase 2 session 2 wave 2A`).

### v0.18.1 — Phase 2 Session 2 wave 2B (2026-05-08) — gameplay-systems (Match-start spawn extended to full RPS roster — 33 units)

- **Match-start spawn now lays out the full Phase 2 RPS triangle.** Per `02e_PHASE_2_SESSION_2_KICKOFF.md` §2 deliverables 1-4 + DoD §3. `main.gd::_spawn_starting_units` extends from 5 Kargar + 5 Piyade + 5 Turan_Piyade (15 units, Phase 2 session 1 wave 2A baseline) to **33 starting units** by appending six new trios after the existing leading sequence: Kamandar / Savar / AsbSavarKamandar (Iran) and TuranKamandar / TuranSavar / TuranAsbSavar (Turan). Existing 5/5/5 anchors are unchanged so previous live-test muscle memory (the Iran Piyade line at Z=-8, Turan Piyade line at Z=+20) still works.

- **Spawn-order determinism preserved.** `Unit.reset_id_counter()` runs first; sequence is Kargar 1..5, Iran Piyade 6..10, Turan Piyade 11..15, Kamandar 16..18, Savar 19..21, AsbSavar 22..24, TuranKamandar 25..27, TuranSavar 28..30, TuranAsbSavar 31..33. Replay-diff cleanliness preserved across the bigger roster.

- **Geometry rationale (the "two opposing armies" read at default zoom).** All Iran spawn positions live at Z<0 (south of origin); all Turan spawn positions at Z>0. The Iran↔Turan Z gap is ≥ 24 units (deliberately further than the wave-2A Piyade gap of ~28) so even Asb-savar's 7.0 attack range still requires a meaningful walk to engage — verifies Moving → Attacking transitions over distance, not just in-range. Within each side the new trios occupy distinct corner clusters: Kamandar NW (X≈-9, Z≈-12 / +24), Savar NE (X≈+9), AsbSavar S/N-center (X≈0, Z≈-15 / +27). Trio-internal spacing is 1.5 units (matches Piyade-line spacing) so a tight box-select drag lands one cluster cleanly without picking up adjacent trios.

- **No new Constants.** Per the kickoff brief — match-start spawn positions are main.gd's own match-config knob, same place Phase 1 session 1's Kargar positions and Phase 2 session 1's Piyade positions live. Constants remain for cross-cutting gameplay tunables (HP, damage, ranges) — not spawn layouts.

- **Cross-feature integration smoke updated.** `tests/integration/test_phase_2_session_1_combat.gd::test_main_tscn_spawns_33_units_correct_teams` updated from the 15/10/5 invariants to 33/19/14 (Iran=5 Kargar+5 Piyade+9 new types; Turan=5 Piyade+9 new types). Mechanical follow-on: the spawn count is the canonical invariant the integration test pins; leaving it at 15 would have locked the project into an outdated reality.

- **Tests.** `tests/unit/test_match_start_spawn.gd` extended from 17 to 33 tests: per-new-type position-array shape (3 entries each), pairwise-distinct positions, Iran-trios-Z-negative + Turan-trios-Z-positive invariant, per-type spawn-count assertions (3 each), team mirror to SpatialAgentComponent for both Iran and Turan new types, full unit_id ordering 1..33. Test count 858 → 879 (+21 net). 876 passing, 3 pre-existing pending (FarrSystem fallback, navmap-not-ready, navmesh-not-ready). Lint clean.

- **Live-game-broken-surface (Experiment 01):**
  1. *Runtime state no unit test exercises:* Each new unit instantiates correctly via PackedScene load + `Node3D` add_child. The dual-init unit_type pattern (each subclass sets unit_type in BOTH `_init` AND `_ready` BEFORE `super._ready()`) survives the @export reset between phases — wave-1A through wave-1C tests already verify each subclass independently, wave-2B trusts that surface. Team field set BEFORE add_child so SpatialAgentComponent's `_ready` mirrors the right value (the `_assert_all_team` helper re-asserts this for each new type).
  2. *Headless can't detect:* Visual readability — does the layout READ as Iran-column-vs-Turan-column at default zoom? Do trios of 3 stand visually apart from the line of 5 Piyade? The Z-staggering (Kamandar/Savar at Z≈-12 vs Piyade at Z=-8 gives front/back separation; AsbSavar at Z≈-15 sits behind both) and the X-spread between corner trios prevents cluster overlap. Color contrast against sandy terrain (the Phase 2 session 1 Farr-gauge contrast lesson) is preserved by each subclass's scene-side material — wave-1A through wave-1C already addressed this at the per-unit level.
  3. *Min interactive smoke test:* Lead boots, sees 33 units split into two visible columns. Box-selects Iran Kamandar trio, right-clicks far Turan Savar trio: Kamandar fires from range, Savar charges in, Savar wins (anti-archer 2.0× × 3 attackers vs 3 fragile archers compounds). Repeat for Piyade vs Savar (1.5×, Piyade should win), Asb-savar vs Piyade (kiting at range 7.0 vs Piyade's 1.5 + 1.2× anti-infantry — Asb-savar should win without being touched if microed).

- **Known Godot Pitfalls applied:**
  - **#7 (multi-agent shared-tree commit-staging race):** wave-2B is a single-agent deliverable on `feat/phase-2-session-2`; no parallel agent on the branch. Pre-staging `git diff --staged --stat` should show only my files (`main.gd`, `test_match_start_spawn.gd`, `test_phase_2_session_1_combat.gd`, ARCHITECTURE.md, BUILD_LOG.md).

  - **#1 (mouse_filter on Control nodes):** N/A — wave-2B does not add new Control nodes.

- **LATER candidates (NEW):**
  - *Spawn-config-as-data when match types diverge.* Currently `main.gd` is the single source-of-truth for "where do units start at scene load." When match types diverge (skirmish-vs-1v1-ladder-vs-tutorial scenarios in Phase 5+), extract spawn positions to a `match_setup.tres` resource keyed by scenario id, attached as a child of Main in main.tscn. Keep main.gd's spawn helper as the consumer of that resource. Threshold: when ≥ 2 distinct spawn layouts ship. Not promoted to L# — single-scenario for now.
  - *Per-type cluster-spawn helper.* `_spawn_starting_units` repeats `for pos in <const>: _spawn_unit(<scene>, pos, <team>)` six times for the new trios. ### v0.18.2 — Phase 2 Session 2 wave 3 (2026-05-08) — qa-engineer (Integration tests for full RPS roster + live combat chain)

- **17 new integration tests in `tests/integration/test_phase_2_session_2_rps_combat.gd`.** Covers the live-game-broken-surface for waves 1+2: the full chain from BalanceData → Unit._apply_balance_data_defaults → CombatComponent fields → UnitState_Attacking._sim_tick → combat._sim_tick → CombatMatrix.get_multiplier() → scaled take_damage_x100. Each test drives real unit scenes via the production EventBus chain.

- **RPS triangle 1v1 outcomes (5 tests).** Piyade vs Savar (1.5× anti-cavalry, Savar HP=0 first in ~300 ticks vs Piyade ~396); Savar vs Kamandar (2.0× cavalry-vs-archer, Kamandar HP=0 first in ~99 ticks vs Savar ~645); Kamandar vs Piyade at range 6.0 (1.5× anti-infantry, Piyade HP=0 via accumulated range-plus-melee DPS); AsbSavar vs Piyade held at range (1.2× kiting advantage, Piyade HP=0); Turan-mirror Piyade vs Savar (symmetric 1.5× fold, TuranSavar HP=0 first). Death detection via `hp_x100 ≤ 0` — `queue_free.call_deferred()` defers node free to process_frame which doesn't run inside SimClock._test_run_tick loops.

- **Turan-fold correctness via live chain (1 test).** Two parallel pairs (Iran Piyade → Iran Savar at X=100; Turan_Piyade → Turan_Savar at X=200) advance 3 ticks simultaneously. HP drops must match within 100 x100 tolerance. If CombatComponent bypassed get_multiplier() and read raw effectiveness dict, Turan keys return 1.0× (no "turan_piyade" row), producing 1000 instead of 1500 scaled damage — detectable divergence.

- **33-unit match-start roster verification (4 tests).** All 33 units have non-empty unit_type (dual-init pattern); all 6 wave-2B types appear × 3 count; Iran trios are TEAM_IRAN, Turan trios TEAM_TURAN; unit_id sequence is 1..33 in spawn order.

- **Kiting-math correctness (2 tests).** AsbSavar at origin vs TuranPiyade at distance 6.0: (a) AsbSavar fires before Piyade closes melee (hp_at_50 < initial_hp, piyade dist > 1.5 at tick 50); (b) pure analytical check verifying shot count and total damage in the kiting window without any unit behavior.

- **Cross-feature 5v5 RPS smoke (1 test).** Loads main.tscn, identifies Iran Piyade cluster (5 units) and Turan Savar cluster (3 units), positions them adjacent, issues focus-fire Attack commands, advances until first Turan Savar reaches HP=0. Asserts ≥1 Savar HP=0 AND ≥1 Iran Piyade still alive. Exercises: FSM transitions, CombatComponent RPS lookup, BalanceData reads, HP decrement — all via the live EventBus path.

- **CombatComponent live-path audit (4 tests).** Live unit scenes (not fixtures): Kamandar 1.5× vs Piyade, Savar 2.0× vs Kamandar, TuranKamandar Turan-fold 1.5× vs TuranPiyade, AsbSavar 1.2× vs Piyade — all reading expected values from balance.tres and asserting exact HP after first hit. Complements wave-2A's fixture-based tests by proving the wiring survives scene instantiation.

- **Tests.** Test count 879 → 896 (+17 net). 893 passing, 3 pre-existing pending (FarrSystem fallback, navmap-not-ready, navmesh-not-ready). Lint clean (0 violations).

- **Live-game-broken-surface (Experiment 01) — wave 3 answers:**
  1. *Runtime state no unit test exercises:* Real `CombatComponent._sim_tick` driven by real `Unit._on_sim_phase` listening to real `EventBus.sim_phase` emitting from real `SimClock`, with real `BalanceData.combat.get_multiplier()` returning the right scaled damage to `take_damage_x100`. Each test exercises the FULL chain.
  2. *Headless can't detect:* Battle FEEL (decisive vs marginal). Visual unit clustering. These are not headless concerns.
  3. *Min interactive smoke analog:* Cross-feature test covers the headless-equivalent of the lead's "5 Piyade vs 3 Savar" DoD scenario.

- **Design note: death detection pattern.** GDScript's `queue_free.call_deferred()` defers the actual node free to end-of-frame. Inside a `for _i in range(N): SimClock._test_run_tick()` loop, process_frame never runs — `is_instance_valid(unit)` stays true even after `hp_x100 = 0`. Correct pattern: detect death via `hp_x100 ≤ 0` (set synchronously at damage-apply time). This is now documented here as a project-wide pattern for outcome-based combat tests. Existing session-1 tests used `is_instance_valid` only in 3-tick guards where death-in-3-ticks is physically implausible (substantial HP + single-hit damage well below max).

- **Commits:** `test(integration): Phase 2 session 2 wave 3 — full RPS roster + live combat chain integration tests`
